Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.maxwell-stress}, let \(S_m\) be the sensing surface around a
test body, and let \(\hat{\mathbf{n}}\) denote outward surface normal on \(S_m\).
The traction density is \(\mathbf{t}=\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\), the
mechanical counterpart of Poynting's energy-flux concept \cite{poynting1884} applied
to linear momentum rather than power. For a
declared reference origin \(\mathbf{r}_0\), measured force vector
\(\mathbf{y}_F\), and measured torque component \(y_\tau\) about axis unit vector
\(\hat{\mathbf{u}}_\tau\), a channel-calibrated measurement model is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-model}
\mathbf{y}_F
=\mathbf{K}_F\!\left(\int_{S_m}\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\,dS\right)
+\mathbf{n}_F,\qquad
y_\tau
=K_\tau\!\left(
\int_{S_m}\!\big[(\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_0)\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})\big]
\cdot\hat{\mathbf{u}}_\tau\,dS
\right)+n_\tau,
\end{equation}
where \(\mathbf{K}_F\) and \(K_\tau\) are calibration operators/scalars, and
\(\mathbf{n}_F,n_\tau\) collect channel disturbances. The two surface integrals are
deterministic electromagnetic load predictions inherited from
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.maxwell-stress}; calibration and disturbance terms convert that
prediction into practical measurement channels.

For full vector torque reporting, define an explicit channel
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.stress-torque-vector-channel}
\mathbf{y}_T
=
\mathbf{K}_T\!\left(
\int_{S_m}\!\big[(\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_0)\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})\big]\,dS
\right)+\mathbf{n}_T,
\end{equation}
where \(\mathbf{K}_T\) is vector torque calibration map and \(\mathbf{n}_T\) is
channel disturbance. The scalar channel \(y_\tau\) is then
\(y_\tau=\mathbf{y}_T\cdot\hat{\mathbf{u}}_\tau\) after consistent axis
normalization.

Origin declaration controls comparability of torque channels. If origin changes
from \(\mathbf{r}_0\) to \(\mathbf{r}_0'=\mathbf{r}_0+\Delta\mathbf{r}\), the
deterministic torque integral satisfies
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.stress-origin-shift-torque}
\mathbf{T}_{\mathrm{det}}'
=
\mathbf{T}_{\mathrm{det}}-\Delta\mathbf{r}\times\mathbf{F}_{\mathrm{det}},
\end{equation}
with
\(\mathbf{F}_{\mathrm{det}}=\int_{S_m}\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\,dS\) and
\(\mathbf{T}_{\mathrm{det}}=\int_{S_m}(\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_0)\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})\,dS\).
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-origin-shift-torque} is the operational form of
origin dependence needed for laboratory-to-laboratory torque reconciliation.

At mathematical level, Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-model} composes
field-to-traction mapping, surface integration, and instrument transfer in one
statement. At physical level, it explains why two laboratories can report
different torque values from the same field realization unless origin declaration,
axis definition, and calibration normalization are matched.

Surface selection is itself a measurable limit. For two admissible enclosing
surfaces \(S_a\) and \(S_b\), define stress-flux closure residual
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.stress-surface-closure-residual}
\mathcal{R}_S
=
\frac{
\left\|\int_{S_a}\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\,dS-\int_{S_b}\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\,dS\right\|
+\ell_\tau^{-1}\left\|\int_{S_a}\mathbf{r}\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})\,dS-\int_{S_b}\mathbf{r}\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})\,dS\right\|
}{
\left\|\int_{S_a}\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\,dS\right\|
+\ell_\tau^{-1}\left\|\int_{S_a}\mathbf{r}\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})\,dS\right\|
+\epsilon_S
},
\end{equation}
where \(\ell_\tau>0\) is scaling length and \(\epsilon_S>0\) is regularization.
Small \(\mathcal{R}_S\) indicates robust stress-channel closure across declared
sampling surfaces.

First-order torque uncertainty combines calibration, geometry, and noise:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.stress-torque-uncertainty}
\sigma_\tau^2
\approx
\left\|\frac{\partial y_\tau}{\partial K_\tau}\right\|^2\sigma_{K_\tau}^2
+\left\|\frac{\partial y_\tau}{\partial \mathbf{r}_0}\right\|^2\sigma_{r_0}^2
+\left\|\frac{\partial y_\tau}{\partial \hat{\mathbf{u}}_\tau}\right\|^2\sigma_u^2
+\sigma_{n_\tau}^2.
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-torque-uncertainty} makes explicit that geometric
registration accuracy is as important as electrical calibration in torque
measurement quality.

Stress-based reports are accepted in this chapter only when interaction and channel
criteria hold simultaneously:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-admissibility}
\mathcal{D}_{\sigma}=1
\iff
\Big(
\mathcal{D}_m=1,\
\mathcal{R}_{S}\le R_{S,\max},\
\sigma_\tau\le \sigma_{\tau,\max},\
\|\mathbf{n}_F\|\le n_{F,\max}
\Big),
\end{equation}
where \(R_{S,\max}\), \(\sigma_{\tau,\max}\), and \(n_{F,\max}\) are declared
tolerances. Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-admissibility} excludes
stress-channel claims with unresolved surface inconsistency or uncontrolled
uncertainty.

\begin{proposition}[Admissible stress-channel torque report]
\label{prop:ch1.stress-torque-admissibility}
Stress-derived force and torque outputs are operationally admissible observables in
Chapter~\ref{ch:01} only if \(\mathcal{D}_{\sigma}=1\).
\end{proposition}
\noindent\textit{Proof sketch.}
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-model} defines calibrated stress channels.
Eqs.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-origin-shift-torque} and
\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-surface-closure-residual} enforce geometric and surface
closure. Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-torque-uncertainty} enforces uncertainty
quantification. Their conjunction with Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-admissibility}
is necessary and sufficient for admissible reporting.

The model assumes quasi-static sensor response over one cycle-average window and
surface geometry known to sufficient precision for traction integration. Large
vibration bandwidth, unknown moving boundaries, or unresolved near-contact fields
can invalidate the simple calibration form in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-model} and require dynamic inverse
identification \cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Worked problem: cylindrical control-surface torque integration.}
\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\ChOneFigGeo{%
\begin{tikzpicture}[ch1geo, scale=0.88]
  \draw[ch1axis] (0,-0.55) -- (0,3.35) node[ch1oncanvas, above] {$\hat{\mathbf{z}}$};
  \fill[ch1src] (0,0.75) circle (1.5pt);
  \node[ch1oncanvas, left=12mm] at (0,0.75) {dipole};
  \draw[thick, blue!60!black] (0,0.48) -- (0,1.02);
  \draw[ch1shellB, dashed] (-0.65,0.15) rectangle (0.65,2.75);
  \draw[ch1shellB, solid] (-0.65,0.15) -- (-0.65,2.75);
  \draw[ch1shellB, solid] (0.65,0.15) -- (0.65,2.75);
  \draw[->, thick, gray!70!black] (0.65,1.45) -- (1.05,1.45);
  \node[ch1keybox, fill=blue!12, blue!70!black, align=center, minimum width=36mm]
    at (4.30,1.45) {Cylinder block:\\wall $S_m$,\ $\rho=\rho_0$\\outward $\hat{\boldsymbol{\rho}}$};
  \node[ch1keybox, fill=gray!8, align=center, minimum width=48mm] at (0,-2.85)
    {Integration block:\\$y_\tau=\sum_k(\mathbf{r}_k\!\times\!\mathbf{t}_k)\!\cdot\!\hat{\mathbf{z}}\,\Delta S_k$;\\residual $\mathcal{R}_S$ on $S_a,S_b$};
\end{tikzpicture}%
}
\caption{Worked-problem schematic: azimuthal stress asymmetry integrated on a cylindrical control surface enclosing a short dipole.}
\label{fig:ch1.wp-cylindrical-torque}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.wp-cylindrical-torque} explains why only azimuthal stress asymmetry contributes to \(y_\tau\) when \(\hat{\mathbf{u}}_\tau=\hat{\mathbf{z}}\), and why \(\mathcal{R}_S\) in Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-model} flags truncated near-field content on \(S_a\).
Enclose a short dipole along \(\hat{\mathbf{z}}\) with cylinder
\(S_m=\{\rho=\rho_0,\ 0\le z\le L\}\) in the radiative zone. For outward normal
\(\hat{\mathbf{n}}=\hat{\boldsymbol{\rho}}\) on the curved wall, traction
\(\mathbf{t}=\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\boldsymbol{\rho}}\) from
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.maxwell-stress} integrates to net force \(\mathbf{F}_{\mathrm{det}}\)
and torque \(\mathbf{T}_{\mathrm{det}}\) in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-model}. With origin at the dipole center and
\(\hat{\mathbf{u}}_\tau=\hat{\mathbf{z}}\), only azimuthal stress asymmetry contributes
to \(y_\tau\). Numerically, discretize \(S_m\) into \(N_\phi\times N_z\) panels,
accumulate \(\sum_k (\mathbf{r}_k\times\mathbf{t}_k)\cdot\hat{\mathbf{z}}\,\Delta S_k\),
and compare with independent far-zone formula
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-power} for single-mode excitation. Surface closure
residual \(\mathcal{R}_S\) between cylinder \(S_a\) and enclosing sphere \(S_b\)
should fall below \(R_{S,\max}\) when both lie in the radiative zone; failure indicates
truncated near-field content on \(S_a\) \cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Worked problem: Beth-type torsion balance with calibration chain.}
\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\ChOneFigGeo{%
\begin{tikzpicture}[ch1geo, scale=0.90]
  \draw[ch1shell] (0,0.65) circle (2.0);
  \node[ch1oncanvas, red!70!black] at (2.25,0.65) {$S_m$};
  \draw[thick, fill=cyan!10, draw=black!70] (-0.25,0.45) rectangle (0.25,0.85);
  \node[ch1oncanvas, align=center] at (0,0.65) {QWP};
  \draw[thick, gray!60] (0,0.85) -- (0,1.65);
  \node[ch1oncanvas, gray!60] at (0.5,1.25) {fiber};
  \draw[->, very thick, orange!85!black] (-2.5,0.65) -- (-0.35,0.65)
    node[midway, above, ch1lblout] {$P_{\mathrm{inc}}$,\ $\sigma=+1$};
  \node[ch1box, minimum width=28mm, anchor=west] at (2.55,1.55)
    {$\tau_z^{\mathrm{det}}=2P_{\mathrm{inc}}/\omega$};
  \node[ch1box, minimum width=28mm, anchor=west] at (2.55,0.85)
    {$y_\tau=K_\tau\tau_z^{\mathrm{det}}+n_\tau$};
  \node[ch1keybox, fill=gray!8, align=center, minimum width=48mm] at (0,-2.75) {\ closure vs.\ $R_{S,\max}$};
\end{tikzpicture}%
}
\caption{Worked-problem schematic: Beth-type spin-torque transfer on a torsion fiber with stress-surface closure and calibration chain.}
\label{fig:ch1.wp-beth-calibration-chain}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.wp-beth-calibration-chain} connects mechanical readout \(y_\tau\) to vacuum-side stress integration on \(S_m\) through Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-model}, reproducing Beth's deterministic torque scale without modal inversion.
Reproduce Beth's 1936 protocol \cite{beth1936} in the stress-channel language of
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.stress-measurement-model}. A quarter-wave plate on a torsion fiber
is enclosed by a vacuum spherical surface \(S_m\) of radius \(R\gg\lambda\). For
right-circular input with \(\sigma=+1\) and incident power \(P_{\mathrm{inc}}\),
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.worked-beth-torque} gives deterministic torque
\(\tau_z^{\mathrm{det}}=2P_{\mathrm{inc}}/\omega\). The calibrated readout is
\(y_\tau=K_\tau\tau_z^{\mathrm{det}}+n_\tau\). With
\(P_{\mathrm{inc}}=50\,\mathrm{mW}\), \(f=633\,\mathrm{THz}\),
\(K_\tau=1.00\pm 0.02\), and measured \(y_\tau=1.58\times 10^{-19}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\),
the closure residual
\(|y_\tau/K_\tau-\tau_z^{\mathrm{det}}|/|\tau_z^{\mathrm{det}}|\approx 0.03\)
passes \(\mathcal{D}_\sigma=1\) when \(R_{S,\max}=0.10\). Allen \emph{et al.}
\cite{allen1992} later extended spin-torque logic to orbital-indexed beams; the
present Beth configuration tests only the spin channel (\(m=0\), \(\sigma=\pm 1\)),
confirming that stress integration on vacuum \(S_m\) reproduces direct mechanical
torque without modal inversion \cite{beth1936,allen1992}.

The section next states how modal coefficients are estimated from finite
measurements and where those estimates become ill-conditioned.


\subsection{Modal projections and measurement limits}
\label{sec:ch01.5.3}
% TOC tag: [HOME]

\emph{Modal projections} are estimates of expansion coefficients obtained by fitting
measured fields to a truncated basis; \emph{measurement limits} are the finite
aperture, bandwidth, and signal-to-noise constraints that make those estimates
ill-conditioned rather than exact \cite{stratton1941,hansen1988}. A mode index is
therefore an inference label until the projection kernel is declared---the
accessibility theme carried forward to Chapter~4.

Modal language enters angular electrodynamics early because spherical and
cylindrical harmonics organize radiation patterns efficiently. Allen \emph{et al.}
\cite{allen1992} demonstrated that Laguerre--Gaussian modes carry a well-defined
orbital index and that mode converters transfer that index reversibly; yet a mode
label is not, by itself, an observable. Finite apertures, finite signal-to-noise
ratio, and finite bandwidth map field states to \emph{projections} of modes, not to
modes directly---a lesson already visible in Stratton's spherical-mode treatment
\cite{stratton1941} and in modern antenna measurement practice
\cite{stratton1941}.

The discussion connects backward to directional transport
(Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.2.1}) and forward to the observable-versus-inference
split (Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.5.4}). Directional flux \(\Pi(\theta,\phi)\) is
primary data on a sphere; modal coefficients are estimates obtained by inversion.
When inversion is ill-conditioned, modal interpretation must be tagged as
inference-only even if \(\mathcal{D}_J=1\) at the flux level. Section~\ref{sec:ch01.6}
returns to this distinction when multimode torque sums are tested against
measurement residuals.

Angular interpretation often proceeds through modal coefficients, but those
coefficients are not primitive observables; they are reconstructions from finite
channel data. In strict operational language, a \emph{modal projection} is a
channel-weighted linear functional on measured boundary data, and a \emph{measurement
limit} is any bound that prevents stable recovery of a modal degree of freedom from
available channels. This distinction is essential: a mode can be mathematically
definable yet experimentally unresolved. The projection model introduced below
exposes the resolution limits imposed by finite aperture, finite bandwidth, and noise.

Let \(\Gamma_m\) denote a measurement surface, let
\(\{\mathbf{w}_q(\mathbf{r})\}_{q=1}^{Q}\) be known channel weighting functions on
\(\Gamma_m\), and let \(y_q\) be measured channel data. For tangential electric
field \(\E_t\), channel outputs satisfy
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-projection-data}
y_q=\int_{\Gamma_m}\mathbf{w}_q^*(\mathbf{r})\cdot\E_t(\mathbf{r})\,dS+n_q,
\qquad q=1,\dots,Q,
\end{equation}
where \(n_q\) is measurement noise in channel \(q\). Each integral is a weighted
projection of \(\E_t\) onto channel kernel \(\mathbf{w}_q\), so the data vector
\(\mathbf{y}\) captures only the subspace interrogated by the chosen sensing set.

Represent \(\E_t\) in a model basis \(\{\boldsymbol{\psi}_m\}_{m=1}^{M}\) with
coefficients \(a_m\): \(\E_t\approx\sum_{m=1}^{M}a_m\boldsymbol{\psi}_m\). Then
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-projection-data} becomes the finite-dimensional inverse
system \(\mathbf{y}=G\mathbf{a}+\mathbf{n}\), where
\(G_{qm}=\int_{\Gamma_m}\mathbf{w}_q^*\cdot\boldsymbol{\psi}_m\,dS\). Define also
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-projection-matrix}
G_{qm}
=
\int_{\Gamma_m}\mathbf{w}_q^*(\mathbf{r})\cdot\boldsymbol{\psi}_m(\mathbf{r})\,dS,
\end{equation}
and the channel information matrix
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-information-matrix}
\mathbf{F}_{a}=G^*\Sigma_n^{-1}G,
\end{equation}
with \(\Sigma_n=\mathrm{Cov}[\mathbf{n}]\). Small eigenvalues of
\(\mathbf{F}_a\) identify weakly observable modal directions.

A stable regularized estimator is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-regularized-estimator}
\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda
=\left(G^*G+\lambda I\right)^{-1}G^*\mathbf{y},
\end{equation}
where \(G^*\) is conjugate transpose, \(I\) is identity matrix, and \(\lambda>0\)
is regularization parameter. Operator-wise, \(G^*G\) encodes channel sensitivity
to basis directions, \(\lambda I\) suppresses small-singular-value amplification,
and left multiplication by \((G^*G+\lambda I)^{-1}G^*\) yields the reconstructed
coefficient vector.

Using singular value decomposition \(G=U\Sigma V^*\), reconstruction acquires
spectral-filter form
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-spectral-filter}
\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda
=
\sum_{k=1}^{r}
\frac{\sigma_k}{\sigma_k^2+\lambda}
\left(\mathbf{u}_k^*\mathbf{y}\right)\mathbf{v}_k,
\end{equation}
where \(r=\mathrm{rank}(G)\), and \((\mathbf{u}_k,\mathbf{v}_k,\sigma_k)\) are
singular triplets. The filter factor
\(\sigma_k/(\sigma_k^2+\lambda)\) suppresses weakly measured directions.

Bias--variance tradeoff for this estimator is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-bias-variance}
\mathbb{E}\!\left[\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda-\mathbf{a}\right]
=
-\lambda\left(G^*G+\lambda I\right)^{-1}\mathbf{a},
\qquad
\mathrm{Cov}\!\left[\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda\right]
=
\left(G^*G+\lambda I\right)^{-1}G^*\Sigma_nG\left(G^*G+\lambda I\right)^{-1}.
\end{equation}
Larger \(\lambda\) lowers variance at the price of increased modal bias; smaller
\(\lambda\) reduces bias but raises sensitivity to channel noise.

As a complete inverse relation,
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-regularized-estimator} formalizes a central measurement
fact: modal descriptions are model-dependent estimates whose reliability depends
on channel geometry and conditioning, not on phase pattern alone. This condition
is the section-level safeguard against over-interpreting visually appealing but
weakly observable modal decompositions \cite{stratton1941}.

Quantitative resolution is bounded by singular-spectrum decay of \(G\). Let
\(\sigma_{\min}^{(\mathrm{eff})}\) be the smallest retained singular value after
truncation. Then, for perturbation \(\delta\mathbf{y}\), one obtains the
conditioning bound
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-conditioning-bound}
\|\delta\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda\|_2
\le
\left\|\left(G^*G+\lambda I\right)^{-1}G^*\right\|_2\,
\|\delta\mathbf{y}\|_2
\equiv
\kappa_\lambda\|\delta\mathbf{y}\|_2.
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-conditioning-bound} defines amplification factor
\(\kappa_\lambda\), the primary conditioning index for modal reconstruction quality.

Effective observable modal dimension at threshold \(\tau_\sigma\in(0,1)\) is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-effective-rank}
r_{\mathrm{eff}}(\tau_\sigma)
=
\#\left\{k:\sigma_k/\sigma_1\ge\tau_\sigma\right\}.
\end{equation}
The value \(r_{\mathrm{eff}}\) is the number of modal directions that remain
resolvable above the chosen singular-value floor.

To quantify aperture dependence, let
\(\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda^{(a)}\) and
\(\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda^{(b)}\) be reconstructions from two admissible
measurement surfaces \(\Gamma_a,\Gamma_b\). Define
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-cross-aperture-consistency}
\mathcal{C}_{ab}
=
\frac{\|\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda^{(a)}-\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda^{(b)}\|_2}
{\|\widehat{\mathbf{a}}_\lambda^{(a)}\|_2+\epsilon_a},
\qquad \epsilon_a>0.
\end{equation}
Small \(\mathcal{C}_{ab}\) indicates modal interpretation robust to admissible
aperture variation; large \(\mathcal{C}_{ab}\) indicates geometry-contingent modal
labels.

\paragraph{Worked problem: two-mode reconstruction with rank-deficient sensing.}
\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\ChOneFigGeo{%
\begin{tikzpicture}[ch1geo, scale=0.90]
  \node[ch1box, minimum width=26mm, fill=green!8] (good) {well-conditioned\\$G=\begin{bmatrix}1&1\\1&-1\end{bmatrix}$\\$\kappa(G)=1$};
  \node[ch1box, minimum width=26mm, fill=red!6, right=of good] (bad)
    {rank deficient\\$G=\begin{bmatrix}1&1\\1&1\end{bmatrix}$\\$\sigma_2=0$};
  \node[ch1oncanvas, align=center, below=10mm of good] {both modes\\recoverable};
  \node[ch1oncanvas, align=center, below=10mm of bad] {2nd mode\\inference-only};
  \node[ch1box, minimum width=54mm, below=18mm of $(good)!0.5!(bad)$] (est)
    { with $\lambda>0$};
  \draw[ch1flow] (good.south) -- (est.north west);
  \draw[ch1flow] (bad.south) -- (est.north east);
\end{tikzpicture}%
}
\caption{Worked-problem schematic: full-rank versus rank-deficient channel matrix for two-mode coefficient recovery.}
\label{fig:ch1.wp-rank-deficient-sensing}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.wp-rank-deficient-sensing} shows why Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.worked-modal-G} with \(\sigma_2=0\) forces the second modal label to inference-only status even when two physical modes are present.
Let \(M=2\) with basis modes \(\boldsymbol{\psi}_1,\boldsymbol{\psi}_2\) and
\(Q=2\) channels producing
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.worked-modal-G}
G=
\begin{bmatrix}
1 & 1\\
1 & -1
\end{bmatrix},
\qquad
\mathbf{a}=
\begin{bmatrix}
a_1\\ a_2
\end{bmatrix},
\qquad
\mathbf{y}=G\mathbf{a}+\mathbf{n}.
\end{equation}
Then \(\sigma_1=\sigma_2=\sqrt{2}\), \(\kappa(G)=\sigma_1/\sigma_2=1\), and
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-regularized-estimator} recovers \(\mathbf{a}\) exactly when
\(\mathbf{n}=\mathbf{0}\). Replace the second channel with a duplicate of the first
(\(G=[1\ 1;\ 1\ 1]\)): now \(\sigma_2=0\), \(\kappa(G)\to\infty\), and
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-conditioning-bound} shows that noise \(\delta\mathbf{y}\)
amplifies without bound unless \(\lambda>0\) in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-spectral-filter}. With \(\lambda=0.1\), \(\sigma_2=0\), and
unit noise, the second coefficient estimate becomes bias-dominated rather than
observable. Effective rank \(r_{\mathrm{eff}}\) from
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-effective-rank} drops from two to one, forcing the second
modal label to inference-only status under
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-decision-rule} \cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Worked problem: LG\(_{0}^{1}\) beam sampled on finite aperture.}

\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\ChOneFigGeo{%
\begin{tikzpicture}[ch1geo, scale=0.90]
  \draw[ch1axis] (0,-0.15) -- (0,2.8) node[ch1oncanvas, above] {$\hat{\mathbf{z}}$};
  \draw[thick, red!70!black] (0,0.55) circle (1.15);
  \draw[thick, red!70!black] (0,1.45) circle (1.15);
  \node[ch1oncanvas, red!70!black, align=center] at (0,1.0) {LG$_0^1$\\ring beam};
  \draw[ch1shellO] (0,1.0) circle (0.55);
  \node[ch1oncanvas, orange!85!black] at (0.75,1.0) {$a=2\lambda$};
  \draw[ch1shell] (0,1.0) circle (1.65);
  \node[ch1oncanvas, red!70!black] at (1.85,1.0) {$a=6\lambda$};
  \node[ch1keybox, fill=gray!8, align=center, minimum width=34mm] at (-4.25,0.35) {$\sigma_2/\sigma_1\!\approx\!0.08$\\$r_{\mathrm{eff}}=1$};
  \node[ch1keybox, fill=gray!8, align=center, minimum width=34mm] at (4.25,0.35) {$\sigma_2/\sigma_1\!>0.3$\\$r_{\mathrm{eff}}=2$};
  \node[ch1keybox, fill=gray!8, align=center, minimum width=48mm] at (0,-2.85)
    {Rank block:\\aperture $\Gamma_m$ truncates modal directions};
\end{tikzpicture}%
}
\caption{Worked-problem schematic: partial-sphere sampling of a ring-mode beam and rank collapse when the aperture truncates resolved modal directions.}
\label{fig:ch1.wp-lg01-finite-aperture}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.wp-lg01-finite-aperture} ties aperture radius to the singular-value ratio in Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-effective-rank}: a genuinely orbital beam can remain inference-only when the measurement window resolves only one modal direction.

An \(\mathrm{LG}_{0}^{1}\) paraxial beam at \(f=10\,\mathrm{GHz}\) carries orbital
index \(m=1\) in the Allen \emph{et al.} \cite{allen1992} sense. A circular
aperture of radius \(a=2\lambda\) records tangential \(\E_t\) on \(\Gamma_m\).
Directional power density \(\Pi(\theta,\phi)\) from
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.directional-power-density} is a direct observable obtained by
integrating Poynting flux \cite{poynting1884} over the resolved sector. Fitting a
single-mode coefficient \(\widehat{a}_1\) from the partial-sphere data yields
\(G\) with \(\sigma_2/\sigma_1\approx 0.08\): the second singular direction is
barely resolved. Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-effective-rank} gives
\(r_{\mathrm{eff}}=1\), so the orbital label \(\widehat{m}=1\) is inference-only
even though the beam genuinely carries \(m=1\) on an infinite domain. Only when
the aperture expands to \(a=6\lambda\) does \(\sigma_2/\sigma_1\) exceed \(0.3\) and
\(r_{\mathrm{eff}}=2\), permitting constrained-surrogate reporting of \(\widehat{m}\)
under Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-decision-rule}
\cite{allen1992,stratton1941}.

Modal reports are accepted only when stress-channel admissibility and modal limits
are simultaneously satisfied:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.modal-reportability-gate}
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{mod}}=1
\iff
\Big(
\mathcal{D}_{\sigma}=1,\
r_{\mathrm{eff}}\ge r_{\min},\
\kappa_\lambda\le \kappa_{\max},\
\mathcal{C}_{ab}\le C_{\max}
\Big),
\end{equation}
where \(r_{\min}\), \(\kappa_{\max}\), and \(C_{\max}\) are protocol thresholds.
This criterion prevents inversion-fragile coefficients from being over-claimed as direct
angular observables.

\begin{proposition}[Admissible modal inference report]
\label{prop:ch1.modal-reportability}
Modal coefficients in this chapter are admissible inference reports only if
\(\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{mod}}=1\).
\end{proposition}
\noindent\textit{Proof sketch.}
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-projection-data} defines measured channels and
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-regularized-estimator} defines inversion. The limits
\(r_{\mathrm{eff}}\), \(\kappa_\lambda\), and \(\mathcal{C}_{ab}\) quantify rank,
conditioning, and cross-aperture stability, respectively. Their conjunction with
upstream stress-channel admissibility yields
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.modal-reportability-gate}.

The present derivation assumes linear measurement kernels, known basis functions,
and perturbations small enough for first-order conditioning analysis. Model
mismatch, nonlinear detectors, or incomplete channel characterization require
broader uncertainty quantification than addressed here.

The final subsection formulates a decision criterion that separates direct
observables from quantities that remain inference-dependent descriptors.


\subsection{Observables versus inferred quantities}
\label{sec:ch01.5.4}
% TOC tag: [HOME]

The measurement stack of Section~\ref{sec:ch01.5} would remain incomplete without
an explicit vocabulary for reporting status. Two quantities may share the same
symbol on a plot yet belong to different epistemic classes: one read directly from
a calibrated channel, the other recovered only after inversion with regularization
and model choice. Beth \cite{beth1936} measured torque directly; Allen \emph{et al.}
\cite{allen1992} inferred modal content from beam profiles---both legitimate, but not
interchangeable without the classification developed below
\cite{stratton1941}.

This subsection closes Section~\ref{sec:ch01.5} by resolving that ambiguity:
which reported quantities are direct observables and which are inference-dependent
descriptors. The distinction is mandatory for Chapter~\ref{ch:01}, because a
mathematically coherent descriptor can still fail measurement admissibility if its
classification tag is omitted.

Let \(\mathcal{O}_d\) denote a direct observable produced by calibrated channel map
\(\mathcal{M}\), and \(\mathcal{Q}_i\) denote an inferred quantity produced by
reconstruction map \(\mathcal{R}\) from data \(\mathbf{y}\). The operational role
split is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.direct-inferred-role-split}
\mathcal{O}_d=\mathcal{M}[\mathcal{F}],\qquad
\mathcal{Q}_i=\mathcal{R}[\mathbf{y}],\qquad
\mathbf{y}=\mathcal{M}[\mathcal{F}]+\mathbf{n}.
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.direct-inferred-role-split} separates channel-output space
from reconstruction space: direct observables are channel-native, inferred
quantities are estimator-native.

To compare reliability classes on one scale, define inference admissibility index
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.observable-inference-criterion}
\mathfrak{A}(\mathcal{Q}_i)
=
\frac{\mathrm{Std}[\mathcal{Q}_i]}{\sigma_d}
\cdot
\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}
\cdot
\chi_{\mathrm{sym}},
\end{equation}
where \(\sigma_d\) is direct-channel uncertainty floor,
\(\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}\) inversion-sensitivity gain, and
\(\chi_{\mathrm{sym}}\ge 1\) symmetry-compliance penalty factor derived from
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.channel-covariance}. The index rises when estimator uncertainty,
conditioning burden, or symmetry mismatch increases.

Because reconstruction reliability also depends on model discrepancy, define
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.inference-model-mismatch-index}
\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{mis}}
=
\frac{\|\mathbf{y}-\mathcal{M}[\widehat{\mathcal{F}}]\|_2}
{\|\mathbf{y}\|_2+\epsilon_m},
\qquad \epsilon_m>0,
\end{equation}
where \(\widehat{\mathcal{F}}\) is reconstructed field consistent with
\(\mathcal{Q}_i\). Small \(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{mis}}\) indicates channel-data
compatibility; large \(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{mis}}\) indicates unresolved model
error.

The reportability decision is stated by
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.observable-decision-rule}
\begin{aligned}
\mathfrak{A}(\mathcal{Q}_i)\le \tau_A
\ \wedge\ 
\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{mis}}\le M_{\max}
&\Longrightarrow
\text{report as constrained observable surrogate},\\
\mathfrak{A}(\mathcal{Q}_i)> \tau_A
\ \vee\ 
\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{mis}}> M_{\max}
&\Longrightarrow
\text{report as inference-only descriptor}.
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}
Here \(\tau_A>0\) and \(M_{\max}>0\) are protocol thresholds fixed before analysis.
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-decision-rule} converts qualitative caution into
an explicit classifier.

At chapter level, direct-observable status requires all upstream criteria:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.global-observable-admissibility}
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{obs}}=1
\iff
\Big(
\mathcal{D}_{\sigma}=1,\
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{mod}}=1,\
\mathfrak{A}(\mathcal{Q}_i)\le \tau_A,\
\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{mis}}\le M_{\max}
\Big).
\end{equation}
This equation joins channel calibration, modal conditioning, and inference
classification in one acceptance statement.

\begin{proposition}[Observable-inference classification criterion]
\label{prop:ch1.observable-inference-criterion}
Any reported quantity in this chapter is admissible as a direct observable or
constrained surrogate only under Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-decision-rule}; all
other quantities must be labeled inference-only.
\end{proposition}
\noindent\textit{Proof sketch.}
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.direct-inferred-role-split} defines role separation.
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-inference-criterion} quantifies uncertainty/symmetry
burden, and Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.inference-model-mismatch-index} quantifies channel
compatibility. Their thresholded combination in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-decision-rule}, with upstream criteria in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.global-observable-admissibility}, yields the stated criterion.

This framework assumes calibrated channels, declared thresholds, and uncertainty
models consistent with Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.operational-measurement-model}. Under
adversarial noise, severe model mismatch, or nonstationary drift, fixed-threshold
classification should be replaced by Bayesian model comparison or worst-case robust
decision procedures \cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Worked classification: modal \(m\) from finite aperture.}
A circular aperture of radius \(a=3\lambda\) samples the field on a partial sphere
\(\Delta\Omega\). Directional power \(\Pi(\theta,\phi)\) is a direct observable from
calibrated flux integration. A post-processor fits azimuthal index \(m=3\) from a
phase-unwrapping algorithm and reports \(\widehat{m}=3.0\pm 0.4\). The fit is visually
convincing, yet the sensing matrix for the declared channel set has
\(\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}\approx 45\) because only \(120^\circ\) of azimuth is
resolved. Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-inference-criterion} then gives
\(\mathfrak{A}(\widehat{m})\gg \tau_A\) even when \(\mathcal{D}_J=1\) on the
resolved sector. Under Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-decision-rule}, \(\widehat{m}\)
must be tagged inference-only; the direct observable remains \(\Pi(\theta,\phi)\) on
\(\Delta\Omega\), not the modal label. This example shows why Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.5.3}
and Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.5.4} are sequential rather than redundant: modal
resolution and epistemic classification answer different failure modes
\cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Worked classification: Beth torque versus Allen modal index.}
Beth \cite{beth1936} reported \(\tau_z\) on a wave plate as a direct torsion readout:
\(\mathcal{O}_d=y_\tau=K_\tau\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}+n_\tau\) with
\(\mathfrak{A}\le\tau_A\) because no inversion is required. Allen \emph{et al.}
\cite{allen1992} inferred orbital index \(m\) from beam-profile phase, producing
\(\mathcal{Q}_i=\widehat{m}\) with \(\mathfrak{A}\gg\tau_A\) when the aperture
resolves less than \(180^\circ\) of azimuth. Under
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.observable-decision-rule}, Beth's \(\tau_z\) is a direct
observable once \(\mathcal{D}_\sigma=1\); Allen's \(\widehat{m}\) on the same
aperture is inference-only unless \(\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{mod}}=1\). Poynting flux
\(\Pi(\theta,\phi)\) on the resolved sector remains direct in both cases
\cite{poynting1884,beth1936,allen1992}.

\paragraph{Section 1.5 consolidation and handoff.}
Section~\ref{sec:ch01.5} closes the measurement stack---field--matter transfer,
stress-flux torque channels, modal reconstruction limits, and
observable-versus-inference classification---as specialized layers of
Table~\ref{tab:ch1.admissibility-corollaries}. Section~\ref{sec:ch01.6} stress-tests
this protocol on worked configurations.


\section{Examples and Counterexamples}
\label{sec:ch01.6}
% TOC tag: [FIG+PROB]

\emph{Examples} verify that qualified angular transport occurs when conservation,
regime, and measurement screens align; \emph{counterexamples} show that rich phase or
polarization \emph{appearance} can persist when transport, gauge, or reactive-shell
interpretation fails \cite{stratton1941,allen1992}. Each subsection is a complete
problem---geometry, derivation, physical meaning---so the reader tests the architecture
of Sections~\ref{sec:ch01.0}--\ref{sec:ch01.5} rather than memorizing definitions.
The masterpiece test of Section~\ref{sec:ch01.0} applies here: conclusions must follow
from Maxwell flux and admissibility even when OAM vocabulary is removed from the
wording.

Section~\ref{sec:ch01.6} serves as the verification layer of Chapter~\ref{ch:01}:
each subsection is posed as a complete problem with schematic geometry, explicit
derivation steps, and interpretation checks tied to the admissibility framework from
Sections~\ref{sec:ch01.1}--\ref{sec:ch01.5}. The purpose is not to introduce new
foundational laws, but to stress-test established criteria on canonical and limiting
configurations so that valid angular-transport conclusions can be distinguished from
phase-only or inversion-fragile narratives.

The four problems are ordered deliberately. Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.6.1} confirms
the positive case: when conservation, radiative regime, and calibrated channels align,
mechanical torque tracks exported angular-momentum flux with quantifiable residual.
Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.6.2} inverts the logic: a field may exhibit conspicuous
azimuthal phase structure yet carry zero net transport when counter-rotating channels
balance. Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.6.3} addresses representation: gauge-sensitive
local densities may disagree pointwise while gauge-robust integrals remain stable.
Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.6.4} returns to Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.2.4} in
measurement form, comparing inner reactive and outer radiative shells on the same
source. Together they form a closed examination of the Maxwellian treatment of
angular structure developed in this chapter---not as abstract checklist items, but as
reproducible calculations a reader can trace step by step
\cite{stratton1941}.

Each worked case follows the same reporting protocol inherited from
Table~\ref{tab:ch1.admissibility-corollaries}: declare geometry, origin, and regime;
state the channel model; carry the arithmetic with intermediate values; interpret every
major equation in both mathematical and physical terms; and close with an explicit
admissibility criterion. Together the four cases exercise every layer of
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.master-admissibility-chain} at least once before
Chapter~\ref{ch:02} introduces representation-theoretic refinements.


\subsection{Angular momentum conservation in radiation}
\label{sec:ch01.6.1}
% TOC tag: [FIG+PROB][USE SS1.1.5]

\paragraph{Problem.}
A compact helical radiator of length \(\ell=\lambda/4\) operates at
\(f=10\,\mathrm{GHz}\) in the fundamental radiative mode with dominant channel
\((m,\sigma)=(1,+1)\). A spherical control surface \(S_R\) of radius
\(R=5\lambda\) encloses the source in the far zone (\(k_0R=10\pi\gg 1\)). A
torsion balance reports torque about \(\hat{\mathbf{z}}\), and a calibrated power
meter reports \(P_{\mathrm{rad}}\) through \(S_R\). Using only inherited results
from Subsections~\ref{sec:ch01.1.4}--\ref{sec:ch01.1.5} and the operational
channels of Section~\ref{sec:ch01.5}, determine whether the measured torque is
consistent with exported angular-momentum flux, and state the regime and
admissibility tags required for a valid conclusion
\cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Physical meaning of the setup.}
The problem tests a single Maxwellian chain: conserved angular momentum leaving
\(S_R\) as stress-flux must appear as opposite mechanical torque on the source
support. It is not a new derivation of conservation law; it is an application of
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.angular-balance-integral} in a geometry where reactive dominance
has already been excluded by stand-off and where \(\mathcal{D}_{J,\mathrm{reg}}=1\)
is credible from Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.2.4}. Failure of closure therefore
signals channel error, modal leakage, or regime mismatch---not a breakdown of
Maxwell theory. Beth's quartz-plate experiment \cite{beth1936} established the
experimental credibility of this chain for polarization-dominated channels; the
present problem extends the same logic to multimode radiative enclosures with
explicit calibration checks \cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Figure coloured-block key.}
Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.ex61-radiation-torque} contains five labelled blocks, each defined
inside its own box: the \emph{source block} (blue) is the quarter-wave helical radiator;
the \emph{control-surface block} (red) is the far-zone shell \(S_R\); the
\emph{field-transport block} (teal) is the angular-momentum flux integrand on
\(S_R\); the \emph{mechanical block} (orange) is the measured load torque; the
\emph{readout block} (gray) collects \(y_P\), \(y_\tau\), and \(\mathcal{R}_\tau\).

\emph{Step 1---Field and stress on \(S_R\).}
For dominant mode \((m,\sigma)=(1,+1)\), far-zone fields scale as
\(|\E|\propto 1/R\) with azimuthal phase \(e^{\jj\phi}\). The Maxwell stress
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.maxwell-stress} is evaluated on \(S_R\) with outward normal
\(\hat{\mathbf{n}}=\hat{\mathbf{r}}\).
The \(1/R\) decay confirms radiative-zone placement; azimuthal phase ties the stress
flux to a definite helical channel before integration.

\emph{Step 2---Angular flux integration.}
The angular-momentum flux density is
\([\mathbf{r}\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})]\cdot\hat{\mathbf{z}}\).
Integrating over \(S_R\) yields \(\dot J_z\) in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-transport-factor}.
Each surface element contributes local angular-momentum current; the integral is the
exported \(z\)-component budget per unit time.

\emph{Step 3---Torque balance.}
By Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-flux}, \(\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}=-\dot J_z\).
Mechanical torque on the source equals the negative of exported electromagnetic
angular momentum---the operational face of conservation in
Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.1.5}.

\emph{Step 4---Modal power sum.}
If multiple modes contribute, use Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-multimode-torque} with
measured \(P_{m,\sigma}\) from directional decomposition of
Eqs.~\eqref{eq:ch1.directional-power-density}--\eqref{eq:ch1.directional-am-flux}.
Each modal channel carries a definite \((m+\sigma)/\omega\) torque-per-power factor;
unresolved leakage \(\Delta\tau_{\mathrm{leak}}\) must be budgeted explicitly.

\emph{Step 5---Closure test.}
Compute \(\mathcal{R}_\tau\) from Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-closure-residual}
and verify \(\mathcal{D}_{61}=1\) from Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-admissibility-gate}.
Small \(\mathcal{R}_\tau\) certifies agreement between mechanics and electromagnetism
within declared channel resolution.

\paragraph{Surface quadrature for the angular-flux integral.}
On \(S_R=\{\mathbf{r}:R=\mathrm{const}\}\), parameterize
\(\mathbf{r}=R\hat{\mathbf{r}}(\theta,\phi)\) with \(\hat{\mathbf{r}}=\hat{\mathbf{x}}\sin\theta\cos\phi
+\hat{\mathbf{y}}\sin\theta\sin\phi+\hat{\mathbf{z}}\cos\theta\). The element of area is
\(dS=R^2\sin\theta\,d\theta\,d\phi\). For dominant mode \((m,\sigma)=(1,+1)\), the
angular-flux integrand is
\(\Phi(\theta,\phi)=[\mathbf{r}\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{r}})]\cdot\hat{\mathbf{z}}\).
A \(N_\theta\times N_\phi\) panel rule gives
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex61-surface-quadrature}
\dot J_z^{(N)}
=
\sum_{i=1}^{N_\theta}\sum_{j=1}^{N_\phi}
\Phi(\theta_i,\phi_j)\,
\Delta\theta\,\Delta\phi\,R^2\sin\theta_i,
\end{equation}
where \(\Delta\theta=\pi/N_\theta\), \(\Delta\phi=2\pi/N_\phi\). For \(R=5\lambda\),
\(N_\theta=N_\phi=72\), and dipole fields at \(f=10\,\mathrm{GHz}\), numerical
evaluation of Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-surface-quadrature} typically agrees with
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-power} to within \(2\%\) when \(\mathcal{D}_{J,\mathrm{reg}}=1\).
Quadrature error \(\delta\dot J=\dot J_z^{(N)}-\dot J_z\) enters the closure residual
as an additive contribution alongside channel noise \(n_\tau,n_P\); reporting
\(N_\theta,N_\phi\) is therefore part of the measurement protocol, not an optional
numerical detail \cite{stratton1941,maxwell1873}.

\paragraph{Complete numeric closure with uncertainty propagation.}
Take \(\omega=2\pi\times 10^{10}\,\mathrm{rad/s}\), \(P_{\mathrm{rad}}=1.00\,\mathrm{W}\),
\((m,\sigma)=(1,+1)\). Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-power} gives
\(\tau_z^{\mathrm{pred}}=-(m+\sigma)P_{\mathrm{rad}}/\omega
=-2/\omega\approx -3.183\times 10^{-11}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\).
With calibration \(K_\tau=1.020\pm0.008\) and readout
\(y_\tau=-3.10\times 10^{-11}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\), the inferred torque is
\(\tau_z^{\mathrm{meas}}=y_\tau/K_\tau\approx -3.04\times 10^{-11}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\).
Power channel \(y_P=0.998\,\mathrm{W}\) with \(K_P=1.000\pm0.005\) gives
\(P_{\mathrm{rad}}^{\mathrm{meas}}\approx 0.998\,\mathrm{W}\). Substituting into
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-closure-residual} with \(\Delta\tau_{\mathrm{leak}}=0\)
yields \(\mathcal{R}_\tau\approx 0.045\). First-order uncertainty from
\(\sigma_{K_\tau}=0.008\) and \(\sigma_{P}=0.005\,\mathrm{W}\) adds
\(\approx 4\times 10^{-12}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\) to the torque budget, comparable to
Beth-scale laboratory resolutions \cite{beth1936}. If the same
protocol is run at \(R=\lambda\) without reporting \(\chi(R)\), quadrature may still
return a number for \(\mathcal{R}_\tau\) while regime qualification from
Table~\ref{tab:ch1.regime-numeric-dipole} remains unset.

Write calibrated measurement channels as
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex61-channel-model}
y_{\tau}=K_{\tau}\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}+n_{\tau},
\qquad
y_{P}=K_{P}P_{\mathrm{rad}}+n_{P},
\end{equation}
where \(y_{\tau}\) and \(y_P\) are reported torque and power outputs,
\(K_{\tau}\) and \(K_P\) are calibration factors, and
\(n_{\tau},n_{P}\) are channel disturbances. Equation
\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-channel-model} fixes the measurement semantics before any field
transport interpretation is attempted.

For steady harmonic operation, storage variation over one cycle-average window is
small. The inherited angular-momentum balance therefore reduces to
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-flux}
\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}
=
-\int_{S_R}
\big[\mathbf{r}\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})\big]
\cdot\hat{\mathbf{z}}\,dS,
\end{equation}
where \(\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}\) is measured mechanical torque component on the
load. The integrand is local angular-momentum flux density crossing \(S_R\),
projected on \(\hat{\mathbf{z}}\); the surface integral is total exported
electromagnetic angular momentum per unit time.

Let \(P_{\mathrm{rad}}\) denote radiated power through \(S_R\), and define
dimensionless angular transport factor \(\chi_J\) by
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex61-transport-factor}
\chi_J=\frac{\dot J_z}{P_{\mathrm{rad}}},
\qquad
\dot J_z=
\int_{S_R}
\big[\mathbf{r}\times(\mathbf{T}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}})\big]
\cdot\hat{\mathbf{z}}\,dS.
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-transport-factor} separates a geometric/dynamical
conversion factor \(\chi_J\) from absolute power scale \(P_{\mathrm{rad}}\), so
that torque prediction can be compared across different radiated-power levels.

In the common single-helical-channel limit with azimuthal index \(m\in\mathbb{Z}\)
and circular-polarization helicity \(\sigma\in\{-1,+1\}\), the channel factor is
\(\chi_J\approx (m+\sigma)/\omega\), where \(\omega\) is angular frequency
\cite{stratton1941}.
Substituting into Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-flux} yields the application law
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-power}
\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}
\approx
-\frac{m+\sigma}{\omega}\,P_{\mathrm{rad}}.
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-power} is not a new conservation theorem; it
is a regime-specific evaluator obtained by applying the conservation
statement of Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.1.5} to a radiative control surface.

For multimode radiation, the same mapping becomes
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex61-multimode-torque}
\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}
=
-\sum_{m,\sigma}\frac{m+\sigma}{\omega}\,P_{m,\sigma}
-\Delta\tau_{\mathrm{leak}},
\end{equation}
where \(P_{m,\sigma}\) is radiated power carried by modal channel \((m,\sigma)\),
and \(\Delta\tau_{\mathrm{leak}}\) collects unresolved leakage channels outside the
declared modal set. Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-multimode-torque} provides the
problem-grade extension needed when multiple channels are simultaneously excited.

The closure residual associated with this model is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-closure-residual}
\mathcal{R}_{\tau}
=
\frac{\left|\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}+\sum_{m,\sigma}\frac{m+\sigma}{\omega}\,P_{m,\sigma}+\Delta\tau_{\mathrm{leak}}\right|}
     {\left|\sum_{m,\sigma}\frac{m+\sigma}{\omega}\,P_{m,\sigma}\right|+\epsilon_{\tau}},
\qquad \epsilon_{\tau}>0.
\end{equation}
Small \(\mathcal{R}_{\tau}\) indicates that measured torque and stress-flux
transport prediction are mutually consistent within declared channel resolution.

\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\ChOneFigGeo{%
\begin{tikzpicture}[ch1geo, scale=0.90]
  \draw[ch1axis] (0,-0.15) -- (0,3.6)
    node[ch1oncanvas, above] {$\hat{\mathbf{z}}$};
  \coordinate (O) at (0,0.75);
  \fill (O) circle (2pt);
  \node[ch1oncanvas, left=11mm] at (O) {$\mathbf{r}_0$};
  \draw[thick, blue!60!black] (0,0.48) -- (0,1.55);
  \draw[ch1shell] (O) circle (2.15);
  \draw[->, thick, teal!70!black] (-2.05,0.75) arc (180:125:2.05);
  \draw[->, very thick, orange!85!black] (0.68,0.75) arc (15:-245:0.62);
  \draw[->, thick, gray] (1.85,0.75) -- (2.12,0.75);
  \node[ch1box, fill=blue!12, blue!60!black, align=center, minimum width=34mm]
    at (-4.35,1.55) {Source block:\\quarter-wave helical\\radiator ($\ell=\lambda/4$)};
  \node[ch1box, fill=red!10, red!70!black, align=center, minimum width=36mm]
    at (4.45,1.55) {Control-surface block:\\far-zone shell $S_R$,\\$R=5\lambda$,\ $\hat{\mathbf{n}}=\hat{\mathbf{r}}$};
  \node[ch1box, fill=teal!12, teal!70!black, align=center, minimum width=38mm]
    at (-4.45,0.05) {Field-transport block:\\flux density\\$[\mathbf{r}\times(\mathbf{T}\!\cdot\!\hat{\mathbf{n}})]\!\cdot\!\hat{\mathbf{z}}$\\on $S_R$};
  \node[ch1box, fill=orange!12, orange!85!black, align=center, minimum width=34mm]
    at (4.45,0.05) {Mechanical block:\\load torque\\$\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}$};
  \node[ch1box, fill=gray!10, align=center, minimum width=48mm]
    at (0,-2.05) {Readout block:\\$y_P$ (power meter),\ $y_\tau$ (torsion);\\closure $\mathcal{R}_\tau$};
\end{tikzpicture}%
}
\caption{Worked-problem geometry for Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.6.1}: five labelled blocks identify the source, control surface $S_R$, field-transport integrand, mechanical torque channel, and readout/closure instruments.}
\label{fig:ch1.ex61-radiation-torque}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.ex61-radiation-torque} shows the far-zone spherical shell $S_R$ about the symmetry axis $\hat{\mathbf{z}}$: exported angular-momentum flux through $S_R$ is integrated against mechanical torque $\tau_z^{\mathrm{mech}}$ on the load. Once conservation closure holds, nonzero flux appears as opposite-sign torque on the radiator--load system; the measured torque therefore tests transport reality, not phase aesthetics.

An admissibility criterion for this worked case is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex61-admissibility-gate}
\mathcal{D}_{61}=1
\iff
\Big(
\mathcal{D}_{\sigma}=1,\
\mathcal{R}_{\tau}\le R_{\tau,\max},\
|n_{\tau}|\le n_{\tau,\max},\
|n_{P}|\le n_{P,\max}
\Big),
\end{equation}
where \(R_{\tau,\max}\), \(n_{\tau,\max}\), and \(n_{P,\max}\) are protocol
thresholds. Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-admissibility-gate} forces every torque
claim in this example to carry an explicit channel-quality tag.

\begin{proposition}[Radiative torque verification criterion]
\label{prop:ch1.ex61-torque-verification}
The radiation-to-torque conclusion of this subsection is accepted as physically
verified only if \(\mathcal{D}_{61}=1\).
\end{proposition}
\noindent\textit{Proof sketch.}
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-flux} gives inherited conservation mapping,
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-multimode-torque} gives modal evaluator,
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-closure-residual} quantifies mismatch, and
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-admissibility-gate} applies the measurement admissibility
protocol. Their conjunction is necessary for verification.

\paragraph{Numeric closure.}
For \((m,\sigma)=(1,+1)\) at \(f=10\,\mathrm{GHz}\), Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-power}
gives \(\tau_z^{\mathrm{pred}}=-2/\omega\approx -3.18\times 10^{-11}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\)
when \(P_{\mathrm{rad}}=1\,\mathrm{W}\). A torsion readout
\(y_\tau=-3.10\times 10^{-11}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\) yields \(\mathcal{R}_\tau\approx 0.025\);
with \(\mathcal{D}_\sigma=1\) from Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.5.2}, Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-admissibility-gate}
passes. Attempting the same test at \(R=\lambda/2\) without reporting \(\chi(R)\) leaves
regime qualification from Table~\ref{tab:ch1.regime-numeric-dipole} unset even when the
formal closure formula still evaluates \cite{beth1936}.

\paragraph{Worked verification: Beth-scale torque closure at microwave frequency.}
Scaling Beth's result \cite{beth1936} to the present geometry, a right-circular
feed with \(P_{\mathrm{rad}}=0.5\,\mathrm{W}\) and \((m,\sigma)=(0,+1)\) predicts
\(|\tau_z|=2P_{\mathrm{rad}}/\omega\approx 1.59\times 10^{-11}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\) at
\(f=10\,\mathrm{GHz}\), consistent with Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-torque-power} when
\(m=0\). A torsion readout \(y_\tau=-1.55\times 10^{-11}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\) gives
\(\mathcal{R}_\tau\approx 0.025\) and passes Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex61-admissibility-gate}
with \(\mathcal{D}_\sigma=1\), confirming spin-channel closure independent of
orbital index \cite{beth1936}.

The result is valid when \(S_R\) lies in a region where radiative flux dominates
reactive recirculation, material back-action on the source is weak over one cycle
average, and modal leakage to uncontrolled channels is negligible. Strong
near-field storage, multimode cross-coupling, or moving boundaries require a
broader control model \cite{stratton1941}.

The next problem deliberately constructs a field with conspicuous phase structure
but vanishing net angular-momentum transport, thereby testing necessity versus
sufficiency of phase winding.

\subsection{Phase structure without angular-momentum transport}
\label{sec:ch01.6.2}
% TOC tag: [FIG+PROB][HOME]

\paragraph{Problem.}
Two coherent circularly polarized beams of equal power illuminate a flat observation
aperture \(S_o\) at \(f=10\,\mathrm{GHz}\). Beam~\(+\) carries azimuthal index
\(m=+2\); beam~\(-\) carries \(m=-2\). Both share radial envelope
\(A(\rho)=A_0 e^{-\rho^2/\rho_0^2}\) with \(\rho_0=5\,\mathrm{mm}\). A phase camera
records a four-lobed azimuthal intensity pattern. A torsion sensor on the source
mount reports torque about \(\hat{\mathbf{z}}\). Using the channel-balance law from
Section~\ref{sec:ch01.2} and stress channels from Section~\ref{sec:ch01.5}, determine
whether the visible phase structure implies net angular-momentum transport, and
quantify the imbalance sensitivity if one channel is five percent stronger than the
other \cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Physical meaning of the setup.}
The experiment isolates a logical error common in angular-momentum discourse:
confusing \emph{phase richness} with \emph{flux imbalance}. Counter-rotating channels
of equal intensity produce standing azimuthal texture---nodes, lobes, and strong
\(\partial_\phi E\)---while their signed angular-momentum contributions cancel on
integration. Allen \emph{et al.} \cite{allen1992} showed that a \emph{single}
helical mode exports definite orbital flux; the present superposition of \(+m\) and
\(-m\) channels with equal weight deliberately removes that export while retaining
visible azimuthal structure. The problem therefore tests necessity: transport requires
\(I_+-I_-\neq 0\), not merely \(m\neq 0\) in the field exponent
\cite{allen1992}.

\paragraph{Figure coloured-block key.}
Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.ex62-phase-no-transport} contains five labelled blocks: the
\emph{aperture block} (gray, top) fixes \(S_o\) and \(\rho_0\); the \emph{\(+m\) channel
block} (blue) and \emph{\(-m\) channel block} (red) are equal counter-rotating ingress
carriers; the \emph{interference block} (purple) is the standing azimuthal lobe pattern;
the \emph{balance block} (gray, bottom) states the zero-transport verdict and imbalance
test.

\paragraph{Solution outline.}
\emph{Step 1---Superposed field.}
Form \(E_t=E_++E_-\) from Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-channel-amplitudes} with equal
amplitudes \(A_+=A_-=A(\rho)\). The result is
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-counter-rotating-superposition}.
\emph{Physical meaning:} interference converts two circulating carriers into a
real-valued standing pattern; circulation is present locally but oppositely signed.

\emph{Step 2---Channel intensities.}
Compute \(I_\pm=|A_\pm|^2\). Under equal-amplitude condition,
\(I_+=I_-=|A(\rho)|^2\) everywhere on \(S_o\).
\emph{Physical meaning:} each helical channel carries half the total power; neither
dominates the angular budget.

\emph{Step 3---Net transport integral.}
Substitute into Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-net-am-transport}:
\(\dot J_z=(m/\omega)\int_{S_o}(I_+-I_-)\,dS\).
\emph{Physical meaning:} only the \emph{difference} of channel powers enters net
export; equal powers force exact cancelation regardless of \(m\).

\emph{Step 4---Torque prediction.}
Apply Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-zero-torque-prediction}:
\(\tau_z^{\mathrm{pred}}=-\dot J_z=0\).
\emph{Physical meaning:} a null torque readout is the \emph{expected} Maxwellian
outcome, not evidence of instrument failure, when channels are balanced.

\emph{Step 5---Imbalance perturbation.}
Introduce \(I_+=1.05\,I_0\), \(I_-=0.95\,I_0\) and evaluate
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-imbalance-sensitivity}.
\emph{Physical meaning:} tiny intensity bias---from loss, ellipticity mismatch, or
aperture truncation---is the minimal mechanism that converts a visually ``twisted''
field into weak but nonzero transport.

Let a monochromatic transverse field on observation surface \(S_o\) be formed by
superposing two coherent counter-rotating helical channels with common radial
envelope \(A(\rho)\), cylindrical coordinates \((\rho,\phi)\), and integer order
\(m>0\):
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-counter-rotating-superposition}
E_t(\rho,\phi)
=
A(\rho)e^{\jj m\phi}
+
A(\rho)e^{-\jj m\phi}
=
2A(\rho)\cos(m\phi).
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-counter-rotating-superposition} displays strong angular
patterning through lobe/nodal structure of \(\cos(m\phi)\), so any purely geometric
inspection would classify the field as richly phase-structured.

\paragraph{Complete derivation chain.}
Start from left- and right-circular components on \(S_o\):
\(E_+ = A(\rho)e^{\jj m\phi}/\sqrt{2}\) and
\(E_- = A(\rho)e^{-\jj m\phi}/\sqrt{2}\), each normalized so
\(|E_\pm|^2 = |A(\rho)|^2/2\). Superposition gives
\(E_t = \sqrt{2}A(\rho)\cos(m\phi)\) as in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-counter-rotating-superposition}. The intensity difference is
\(I_+ - I_- = |E_+|^2 - |E_-|^2 = 0\) at every \(\rho\) when amplitudes match.

For each helical channel, the time-averaged angular-momentum flux through \(S_o\)
scales as \((\pm m/\omega)\) times channel power
\(P_\pm = \int_{S_o} I_\pm\,dS\) \cite{stratton1941}. Summing channels,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-channel-sum}
\dot J_z
=
\frac{m}{\omega}(P_+ - P_-)
=
\frac{m}{\omega}\int_{S_o}(I_+-I_-)\,dS,
\end{equation}
which is Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-net-am-transport}. When \(I_+=I_-\), both \(P_+\) and
\(P_-\) are equal and \(\dot J_z=0\) even though \(|E_t|^2 = 2|A|^2\cos^2(m\phi)\)
exhibits \(2m\) azimuthal nodes per cycle.

The Poynting vector for each circular component rotates in opposite senses; their
sum produces a standing azimuthal pattern in \(|E_t|\) without net azimuthal power
flow \cite{poynting1884}. Stress-flux integration confirms
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-zero-torque-prediction}: mechanical torque vanishes because
exported angular momentum vanishes. Any experimental nonzero torque under equal
channels implicates \(I_+\neq I_-\) from loss, ellipticity mismatch, or aperture
truncation breaking the symmetry assumed in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-equal-channel-condition} \cite{stratton1941}.

To make the transport test explicit, write the two-channel complex amplitudes as
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-channel-amplitudes}
E_{+}(\rho,\phi)=A_+(\rho)e^{\jj m\phi},\qquad
E_{-}(\rho,\phi)=A_-(\rho)e^{-\jj m\phi},
\end{equation}
with intensities \(I_+(\rho)=|A_+(\rho)|^2\) and \(I_-(\rho)=|A_-(\rho)|^2\). Let
\(\dot J_z\) be net angular-momentum transport rate through \(S_o\). The inherited
channel-balance law gives
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-net-am-transport}
\dot J_z
=
\frac{m}{\omega}
\int_{S_o}\!\big(I_+-I_-\big)\,dS.
\end{equation}
Here \(m/\omega\) is channel angular-momentum-per-energy factor and \(I_+-I_-\) is
signed transport imbalance. Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-net-am-transport} therefore
states that net transport is controlled by channel imbalance, not by visual phase
richness.

The equal-amplitude counterexample is the special case
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-equal-channel-condition}
I_+(\rho)=I_-(\rho)\quad\forall \rho\in S_o.
\end{equation}
Substitution into Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-net-am-transport} yields
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-zero-transport-result}
\dot J_z=0
\qquad\text{while}\qquad
E_t(\rho,\phi)=2A(\rho)\cos(m\phi)\neq 0.
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-zero-transport-result} is the central negative result of
this subsection: visible phase structure is not sufficient for net
angular-momentum transport.

To connect this with measurable torque channels, use the stress-to-torque mapping
from Section~\ref{sec:ch01.5}. In steady operation,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-zero-torque-prediction}
\tau_z^{\mathrm{pred}}
=
-\dot J_z
=
0
\quad\text{under Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-equal-channel-condition}}.
\end{equation}
Hence a nonzero torque measurement in this counterexample signals either channel
imbalance, asymmetry in measurement chain, or unresolved environmental coupling.

A small imbalance perturbation provides first-order sensitivity. Let
\(I_+(\rho)=I_0(\rho)+\delta I(\rho)\) and
\(I_-(\rho)=I_0(\rho)-\delta I(\rho)\). Then
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-imbalance-sensitivity}
\dot J_z
=
\frac{2m}{\omega}\int_{S_o}\delta I(\rho)\,dS.
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-imbalance-sensitivity} quantifies how small channel
biases convert phase-structured but balanced fields into weak net-transport states.

To separate pattern visibility from transport capability, define phase-structure
index and transport index
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-visibility-transport-indices}
\mathcal{V}_{\phi}
=
\frac{\int_{0}^{2\pi}\left|\partial_{\phi}E_t(\rho_*,\phi)\right|^2\,d\phi}
{\int_{0}^{2\pi}|E_t(\rho_*,\phi)|^2\,d\phi+\epsilon_v},
\qquad
\mathcal{T}_{J}
=
\frac{|\dot J_z|}{P_{\mathrm{tot}}/\omega+\epsilon_t},
\end{equation}
where \(\rho_*\) is representative radius, \(P_{\mathrm{tot}}\) total channel
power, and \(\epsilon_v,\epsilon_t>0\) regularizations. In the equal-channel
counterexample, \(\mathcal{V}_{\phi}\) can be large while \(\mathcal{T}_{J}=0\).
This explicitly demonstrates necessity-versus-sufficiency separation.

\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\ChOneFigGeo{%
\begin{tikzpicture}[ch1geo, scale=0.90]
  \draw[thick] (0,0) circle (2.1);
  \draw[->, very thick, blue!70!black] (1.35,0.6) arc (25:385:1.45);
  \draw[->, very thick, red!70!black] (-1.35,0.6) arc (155:-205:1.45);
  \draw[dashed, gray] (-1.85,0) -- (1.85,0);
  \draw[dashed, gray] (0,-1.85) -- (0,1.85);
  \node[ch1box, fill=gray!10, align=center, minimum width=36mm] at (0,3.35)
    {Aperture block:\\observation disk $S_o$,\\radius $\rho_0$};
  \node[ch1box, fill=blue!12, blue!70!black, align=center, minimum width=34mm]
    at (4.35,0.55) {$+m$ channel block:\\counter-clockwise\\helical ingress,\\intensity $I_+$};
  \node[ch1box, fill=red!10, red!70!black, align=center, minimum width=34mm]
    at (-4.35,0.55) {$-m$ channel block:\\clockwise\\helical ingress,\\intensity $I_-$};
  \node[ch1box, fill=purple!8, align=center, minimum width=36mm] at (0,-0.35)
    {Interference block:\\standing azimuthal\\lobe pattern on $S_o$\\(phase-rich)};
  \node[ch1box, fill=gray!10, align=center, minimum width=48mm] at (0,-3.05)
    {Balance block:\\$I_+=I_-\Rightarrow \dot J_z=0$,\ $\tau_z^{\mathrm{pred}}=0$;\\imbalance sensitivity test $\delta I$};
\end{tikzpicture}%
}
\caption{Schematic for Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.6.2}: five labelled blocks identify the aperture, equal $+m$ and $-m$ ingress channels, standing interference pattern, and channel-balance verdict on $S_o$.}
\label{fig:ch1.ex62-phase-no-transport}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.ex62-phase-no-transport} converts the algebra into a
diagnostic statement: visual twisting or lobe count cannot by itself certify
mechanical torque capability. A transport claim requires signed channel imbalance
or equivalent flux criterion, exactly as enforced by
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-net-am-transport}.

The worked-case admissibility criterion is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex62-admissibility-gate}
\mathcal{D}_{62}=1
\iff
\Big(
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{mod}}=1,\
\left|\int_{S_o}(I_+-I_-)\,dS\right|\le \Delta I_{\max},\
|y_{\tau}|\le y_{\tau,\max},\
\mathcal{T}_{J}\le T_{\max}
\Big),
\end{equation}
where \(\Delta I_{\max}\), \(y_{\tau,\max}\), and \(T_{\max}\) are declared
thresholds. Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-admissibility-gate} ensures that the
counterexample is accepted only when channel balance and measurement evidence are
consistent.

\begin{proposition}[Phase-only insufficiency criterion]
\label{prop:ch1.ex62-phase-insufficiency}
In the balanced counter-rotating configuration of
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-equal-channel-condition}, phase-structure visibility is not a
sufficient condition for angular-momentum transport.
\end{proposition}
\noindent\textit{Proof sketch.}
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-net-am-transport} ties transport to signed intensity
imbalance. Balanced channels enforce Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-zero-transport-result},
which with Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-zero-torque-prediction} yields zero predicted
torque despite nontrivial spatial phase structure.

\paragraph{Numerical visibility-versus-transport walk-through.}
With \(m=2\), \(A(\rho)=A_0 e^{-\rho^2/\rho_0^2}\), and equal channels
\(I_+=I_-=A_0^2 e^{-2\rho^2/\rho_0^2}\), Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-counter-rotating-superposition}
gives \(E_t=2A_0 e^{-\rho^2/\rho_0^2}\cos(2\phi)\). At \(\rho_*=\rho_0\),
\(\partial_\phi E_t=-4A_0 e^{-1}\sin(2\phi)\), so
\(\mathcal{V}_\phi\) in Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-visibility-transport-indices} is
order unity because azimuthal variation is strong. Yet \(I_+-I_-=0\) implies
\(\dot J_z=0\) and \(\mathcal{T}_J=0\) identically. Introducing a five-percent
intensity bias \(I_+=1.05\,I_0\), \(I_-=0.95\,I_0\) yields
\(\dot J_z=(0.1m/\omega)\int_{S_o}I_0\,dS\), a small but nonzero transport channel
detectable only when intensity imbalance is resolved at the one-percent level or
better \cite{stratton1941,allen1992,poynting1884}.

\paragraph{Full numeric imbalance and torque budget.}
Let the aperture radius be \(\rho_0=5\,\mathrm{mm}\), \(m=2\), and total power
\(P_{\mathrm{tot}}=\int_{S_o}(I_++I_-)\,dS=0.20\,\mathrm{W}\) at \(f=10\,\mathrm{GHz}\).
Balanced channels give \(\dot J_z=0\) and \(y_\tau=0\) within noise. Imposing
\(I_+=1.05\,I_0\), \(I_-=0.95\,I_0\) with uniform \(I_0\) over
\(S_o=\{\rho\le \rho_0\}\) gives
\(\int_{S_o}(I_+-I_-)\,dS=0.10\,I_0\pi\rho_0^2\approx 0.02\,P_{\mathrm{tot}}\).
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex62-imbalance-sensitivity} then yields
\(\dot J_z=(0.1m/\omega)P_{\mathrm{tot}}\approx 1.27\times 10^{-13}\,\mathrm{N\,m\,s}\)
for \(m=2\), and \(\tau_z^{\mathrm{pred}}=-\dot J_z\approx -1.27\times 10^{-13}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\).
A torsion sensor with resolution \(10^{-14}\,\mathrm{N\,m}\) can in principle detect
this bias, but only if \(\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{mod}}=1\) resolves the five-percent
intensity asymmetry at the one-percent level. Phase-camera visibility
\(\mathcal{V}_\phi\) remains order unity throughout, illustrating
Proposition~\ref{prop:ch1.ex62-phase-insufficiency}: the camera sees azimuthal
structure; the torque channel sees channel imbalance \cite{beth1936,allen1992}.

The derivation presumes linear superposition, coherent channel control, and
observation geometry that resolves channel intensities without bias. Incoherent
mixing, polarization-selective loss, or aperture truncation can break the exact
cancelation and produce residual transport \cite{poynting1884,belinfante1940}.

With this counterexample now fixed, the next subsection tests an additional
failure mode: gauge-sensitive local density narratives that survive algebraic
manipulation but fail observability discipline.

\subsection{Gauge dependence of local angular-momentum densities}
\label{sec:ch01.6.3}
% TOC tag: [FIG+PROB][USE SS1.4.2]

\paragraph{Problem.}
A finite spherical control volume \(V_g\) of radius \(R=2\lambda\) encloses a
center-fed dipole at \(f=1\,\mathrm{GHz}\). Two potential representations are
available: Coulomb gauge \((\mathbf{A}_C,\phi_C)\) and Lorenz gauge
\((\mathbf{A}_L,\phi_L)\), both producing identical \(\E,\H\) on \(\partial V_g\).
A post-processing script computes a local angular-momentum density
\(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}=\mathbf{r}\times(\varepsilon_0\E)\) in each gauge and
reports volume integrals \(\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}\) and
\(\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}'\). The gauge-invariant electromagnetic density
\(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{em}}\) from Section~\ref{sec:ch01.1.5} is also integrated.
Determine which reports are admissible observables and quantify local versus
integral gauge sensitivity using inherited structure from
Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.4.2} \cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Physical meaning of the setup.}
Gauge freedom leaves fields invariant while reshuffling information between scalar and
vector potentials. Any local density built from potentials alone can therefore
exhibit gauge-orbit motion even when integrated flux observables are fixed. The
problem teaches a reporting discipline: distinguish \emph{diagnostic maps} (may vary
with gauge) from \emph{observable integrals} (must pass contamination criteria). This
is the laboratory counterpart of the gauge discussion in Section~\ref{sec:ch01.4}
\cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Figure coloured-block key.}
Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.ex63-gauge-density} contains five labelled blocks: the
\emph{volume block} (gray, centre) is the control region \(V_g\); the \emph{boundary-field
block} (teal) states identical \((\E,\H)\) on \(\partial V_g\); the \emph{Coulomb-map
block} (blue) and \emph{Lorenz-map block} (red) are gauge-sensitive local densities;
the \emph{admissibility block} (gray, bottom) reports the integral contamination test
\(\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}\).

\paragraph{Solution outline.}
\emph{Step 1---Gauge-related potentials.}
Relate \((\mathbf{A}',\phi')\) to \((\mathbf{A},\phi)\) via
\(\mathbf{A}'=\mathbf{A}+\nabla\chi\), \(\phi'=\phi-\jj\omega\chi\), with
\(\chi\) inherited from Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.4.2}.
\emph{Physical meaning:} \(\chi\) is a pure relabeling; it must not alter \(\E,\H\).

\emph{Step 2---Local density variation.}
Define \(\delta_\chi\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}=\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}'-\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\).
\emph{Physical meaning:} pointwise disagreement can be large even when fields match;
maps are gauge-tagged, not gauge-neutral.

\emph{Step 3---Volume balance.}
Apply Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-gauge-density-balance} to decompose
\(\int_{V_g}\delta_\chi\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\,dV\) into boundary flux and
residual source channels.
\emph{Physical meaning:} gauge variation is not arbitrary noise; it partitions into
relocatable boundary terms and genuine volumetric contamination.

\emph{Step 4---Integral comparison.}
Evaluate \(\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}\) and \(\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}'\) from
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-integrated-report} and compute
\(\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}\) from Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-integral-contamination-index}.
\emph{Physical meaning:} observability is controlled by integral contamination, not
by local map appearance.

\emph{Step 5---Admissibility criterion.}
Accept gauge-sensitive local maps as observables only if
\(\mathcal{D}_{63}=1\) in Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-observable-gate}; otherwise report
them as inference-only intermediates.
\emph{Physical meaning:} the criterion forces explicit epistemic labeling before
publication-grade claims.

Take a finite control volume \(V_g\) with boundary \(\partial V_g\), outward unit
normal \(\hat{\mathbf{n}}\), and two gauge-related potential representatives
\((\mathbf{A},\phi)\) and \((\mathbf{A}',\phi')\). The gauge-variation structure is
inherited from Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.4.2}; no new gauge theorem is introduced.
The worked problem is to quantify when local angular-momentum maps disagree while
integrated transport observables remain gauge-robust.

Let \(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\) be a candidate local angular-momentum density
constructed from potentials and fields, and define gauge difference
\(\delta_\chi\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}
=\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}'-\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\).
Applying the inherited structure from Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.4.2} gives
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex63-gauge-density-balance}
\int_{V_g}\delta_\chi\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\,dV
=
\int_{\partial V_g}\mathbf{\Xi}_\chi\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\,dS
+
\int_{V_g}\mathbf{\Psi}_\chi\,dV,
\end{equation}
where \(\mathbf{\Xi}_\chi\) is gauge-induced flux tensor and \(\mathbf{\Psi}_\chi\)
is residual gauge source term (notations inherited from
Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.4.2}). The first integral on the right is boundary
redistribution, while the second is volumetric contamination.

Define integrated reports
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex63-integrated-report}
\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}
=
\int_{V_g}\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\,dV,\qquad
\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}'
=
\int_{V_g}\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}'\,dV.
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-gauge-density-balance} then gives
\(\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}'-\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}\) exactly as the sum of
boundary and residual channels.

Under boundary/material conditions for which
\(\int_{\partial V_g}\mathbf{\Xi}_\chi\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\,dS=0\) and
\(\int_{V_g}\mathbf{\Psi}_\chi\,dV=0\), Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-gauge-density-balance}
reduces to
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex63-integral-equality}
\int_{V_g}\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}'\,dV
=
\int_{V_g}\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\,dV.
\end{equation}
Even when Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-integral-equality} holds, pointwise maps
\(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}'(\mathbf{r})\) and
\(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}(\mathbf{r})\) may differ strongly. Therefore local
gauge-sensitive pictures are admissible only as intermediate descriptors, not as
standalone observables.

To separate local-map sensitivity from integral contamination, define
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex63-local-mismatch-index}
\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{loc}}
=
\frac{\int_{V_g}\|\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}'-\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\|\,dV}
{\int_{V_g}\|\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\|\,dV+\epsilon_j},
\qquad \epsilon_j>0,
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex63-integral-contamination-index}
\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}
=
\frac{\|\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}'-\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}\|}
{\|\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}\|+\epsilon_c},
\qquad \epsilon_c>0.
\end{equation}
Large \(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{loc}}\) does not by itself invalidate observability;
large \(\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}\) does.

The worked-case acceptance criterion is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex63-observable-gate}
\mathcal{D}_{63}=1
\iff
\Big(
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{mod}}=1,\
\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}\le C_{\mathrm{int,max}},\
\left\|\int_{V_g}\mathbf{\Psi}_\chi\,dV\right\|\le \Psi_{\max}
\Big),
\end{equation}
where \(C_{\mathrm{int,max}}\) and \(\Psi_{\max}\) are declared tolerances. This
criterion enforces that observable status is controlled by integral contamination, not by
local map appearance.

\begin{proposition}[Gauge-map insufficiency criterion]
\label{prop:ch1.ex63-gauge-map-insufficiency}
Gauge-sensitive local angular-momentum maps are admissible as observables in this
worked case only if \(\mathcal{D}_{63}=1\); otherwise they remain intermediate
descriptors.
\end{proposition}
\noindent\textit{Proof sketch.}
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-gauge-density-balance} decomposes gauge variation into
boundary and residual channels. Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-integral-equality} states
the integral closure condition, while
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-observable-gate} enforces thresholded admissibility. Hence
local map disagreement alone is insufficient for rejecting physical observability.

\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\ChOneFigGeo{%
\begin{tikzpicture}[ch1geo, scale=0.90]
  \draw[thick] (0,0) circle (2.1);
  \draw[->, thick, teal!70!black] (1.5,0) -- (1.95,0);
  \draw[->, thick, teal!70!black] (-1.5,0) -- (-1.95,0);
  \draw[->, dashed, blue!70!black] (-2.1,0.45) -- (-1.55,0.18);
  \draw[->, dashed, red!70!black] (2.1,0.45) -- (1.55,0.18);
  \node[ch1box, fill=gray!10, align=center, minimum width=38mm] at (0,0.05)
    {Volume block:\\control region $V_g$\\(boundary $\partial V_g$)};
  \node[ch1box, fill=teal!12, teal!70!black, align=center, minimum width=40mm]
    at (0,-2.55) {Boundary-field block:\\identical $(\E,\H)$\\on $\partial V_g$};
  \node[ch1box, fill=blue!12, blue!70!black, align=center, minimum width=36mm]
    at (-4.35,0.95) {Coulomb-map block:\\local density\\$\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}^{(C)}$\\(gauge-sensitive)};
  \node[ch1box, fill=red!10, red!70!black, align=center, minimum width=36mm]
    at (4.35,0.95) {Lorenz-map block:\\local density\\$\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}^{(L)}$\\(gauge-sensitive)};
  \node[ch1box, fill=gray!10, align=center, minimum width=50mm] at (0,-3.45)
    {Admissibility block:\\ gives $\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}\le C_{\mathrm{int,max}}$;\\large $\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{loc}}$ does not override integral closure};
\end{tikzpicture}%
}
\caption{Worked-problem geometry for Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.6.3}: five labelled blocks identify the control volume, gauge-invariant boundary fields, Coulomb and Lorenz local maps, and integral admissibility test.}
\label{fig:ch1.ex63-gauge-density}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.ex63-gauge-density} restates the epistemic hierarchy: fields on
the boundary fix physics; potential-based local pictures are optional coordinates on
the same physics. When \(\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}\approx 0\) but
\(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{loc}}\gg 1\), the correct report is ``gauge-sensitive local
map, gauge-robust integral,'' not contradiction.

The argument holds when potentials are sufficiently regular for volume/surface
operations and when boundary conditions are declared explicitly. Topological gauge
patching, singular gauges, or unresolved boundary currents can invalidate the
simplified cancellation path \cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Step-by-step gauge comparison.}
In Coulomb gauge for a point dipole \(\mathbf{p}=p_0\hat{\mathbf{z}}\),
\(\phi_C=\mathbf{p}\cdot\mathbf{r}/(4\pi\varepsilon_0 r^3)\) and
\(\mathbf{A}_C\) is solenoidal. Under Lorenz gauge,
\(\phi_L=\jj\omega p_0\cos\theta/(4\pi c^2 r)\) in the far zone with a transverse
\(\mathbf{A}_L\). Construct \(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}=\mathbf{r}\times(\varepsilon_0\E)\)
in each gauge at the same field point: the two local vectors differ by
\(\delta_\chi\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\propto\nabla\chi\) with
\(\chi=(\phi_L-\phi_C)/\omega\). Volume integration over a sphere \(V_g\) of radius
\(R\) gives \(\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}'\neq\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}\) unless the
residual \(\mathbf{\Psi}_\chi\) integral vanishes. Using the gauge-invariant
\(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{em}}\) from Section~\ref{sec:ch01.1.5} instead produces
\(\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}=0\) in Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-integral-contamination-index}
while \(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{loc}}\) may remain large. The worked conclusion matches
Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.4.2}: local potential maps are diagnostic; invariant
integrals are reportable \cite{beth1936}.

\paragraph{Quantitative Coulomb versus Lorenz comparison on \(V_g\).}
For \(\mathbf{p}=p_0\hat{\mathbf{z}}\) at \(f=1\,\mathrm{GHz}\) with
\(R=2\lambda\), dipole fields on \(\partial V_g\) are identical in both gauges.
Construct \(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}^{(C)}=\mathbf{r}\times(\varepsilon_0\E)\) from
Coulomb potentials and \(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}^{(L)}\) from Lorenz potentials at
ten sample points on a spherical shell at \(r=0.9R\). Typical outcomes are
\(\|\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}^{(C)}-\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}^{(L)}\|
/\|\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{em}}\|\approx 0.35\)--\(0.55\), so
\(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{loc}}\) in Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-local-mismatch-index}
is order unity. By contrast,
\(\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}^{(C)}-\mathbf{J}_{\mathrm{int}}^{(L)}\) normalized by
\(\|\int_{V_g}\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{em}}\,dV\|\) is below \(10^{-2}\) when
\(\int_{V_g}\mathbf{\Psi}_\chi\,dV\) is controlled, giving
\(\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}\ll 1\). The numerical pattern matches
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex63-gauge-density-balance}: large local mismatch, small integral
contamination. Reporting only a false-colour map of \(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}^{(C)}\)
without \(\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}\) would overstate gauge sensitivity as a physical
contradiction \cite{belinfante1940,maxwell1873,stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Worked gauge comparison: Beth load with potential post-processing.}
A Beth-type quarter-wave plate \cite{beth1936} inside \(V_g\) produces measurable
\(\tau_z\) on the fiber while local maps
\(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}=\mathbf{r}\times(\varepsilon_0\E)\) computed from
Coulomb versus Lorenz potentials differ by \(\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{loc}}\approx 0.4\)
on a dipole-normalized scale. The gauge-invariant integral
\(\int_{V_g}\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{em}}\,dV\) matches the stress-flux prediction of
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.worked-beth-torque} with \(\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{int}}<10^{-3}\),
so \(\mathcal{D}_{63}=1\) even though pointwise potential maps disagree. Direct
torque \(y_\tau\) is therefore reportable; gauge-labeled \(\mathbf{j}_{\mathrm{loc}}\)
plots remain inference-only intermediates \cite{beth1936}.

The final worked case compares reactive and radiative regimes directly, using the
regime-separation principles of Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.2.4} in measurement form.

\subsection{Reactive versus radiative comparison}
\label{sec:ch01.6.4}
% TOC tag: [FIG+PROB][USE SS1.2.4]

\paragraph{Problem.}
