A center-fed \(\lambda/2\) dipole radiates at \(f=1\,\mathrm{GHz}\). Two concentric
spherical sensor shells are deployed: inner \(S_{r_1}\) at \(kr_1=0.5\) and outer
\(S_{r_2}\) at \(kr_2=5\). On each shell, calibrated channels report active power
\(y_{P,k}\), reactive power \(y_{Q,k}\), and torque magnitude \(y_{\tau,k}\) about
\(\hat{\mathbf{z}}\). Using regime indices from Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.2.4}, classify
each shell as storage-diagnostic or export-diagnostic, compute
\(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_k)\), \(\mathcal{C}_\tau\), and gated efficiency
\(\eta_\tau(r_k)\), and verify \(\mathcal{D}_{64}=1\)
\cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Physical meaning of the setup.}
The two-shell protocol mirrors what happens when one laboratory measures ``angular
momentum'' in the reactive near zone and another measures torque in the far zone.
Both may record structured phase and polarization, yet Maxwellian interpretation
differs: inner-shell data primarily diagnose oscillatory storage exchange; outer-shell
data test export-compatible torque channels. Without explicit \(\mathcal{R}_Q\)
comparison, apparent disagreement is often a regime error, not a physics conflict
\cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Figure coloured-block key.}
Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.ex64-regime-comparison} contains four labelled blocks: the
\emph{source block} (gray) is the centre-fed dipole; the \emph{inner-shell block}
(orange) is the reactive surface \(S_{r_1}\) with storage circulation;
the \emph{outer-shell block} (blue) is the radiative surface \(S_{r_2}\) with outward
export; the \emph{readout block} (gray, bottom) lists shell channels and closure
\(\mathcal{D}_{64}\).

\paragraph{Solution outline.}
\emph{Step 1---Surface functionals.}
Evaluate Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-power-functionals} on \(S_{r_1}\) and \(S_{r_2}\).
\emph{Physical meaning:} \(P(r)\) is irreversible export; \(Q(r)\) is oscillatory
storage circulation---the reactive-radiative split of Section~\ref{sec:ch01.2.4}.

\emph{Step 2---Regime ratio.}
Compute \(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_k)=|Q(r_k)|/(|P(r_k)|+\epsilon_P)\) from
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-reactive-ratio}.
\emph{Physical meaning:} \(\mathcal{R}_Q\gg 1\) flags reactive dominance where phase
texture can mislead; \(\mathcal{R}_Q\ll 1\) permits export interpretation.

\emph{Step 3---Torque contrast.}
Form \(\mathcal{C}_\tau=|\tau_z(r_2)|/(|\tau_z(r_1)|+\epsilon_\tau)\) from
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-torque-contrast}.
\emph{Physical meaning:} strong outer-to-inner torque contrast confirms that
transport-capable readouts emerge only after crossing the reactive shell.

\emph{Step 4---Gated efficiency.}
Apply Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-gated-efficiency} with factor
\(1/(1+\mathcal{R}_Q)\) to suppress false efficiency in reactive zones.
\emph{Physical meaning:} dividing torque by power alone overstates transport
capability when \(|Q|\gg |P|\).

\emph{Step 5---Trend and criterion.}
Evaluate \(\mathcal{T}_{12}\) from Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-trend-consistency} and
verify \(\mathcal{D}_{64}=1\) in Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-regime-admissibility}.
\emph{Physical meaning:} admissible regime discrimination requires both shells to
occupy their expected classes and the transition trend to be internally consistent.

Let \(S_{r_1}\) and \(S_{r_2}\) be concentric spherical observation surfaces,
with radii \(r_1<r_2\), centered on the same source. The objective is to compare
angular-structure interpretation in a reactive-dominant surface \(S_{r_1}\) and a
radiative-dominant surface \(S_{r_2}\), using the regime logic inherited from
Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.2.4}.

Consider a half-wave dipole at \(ka=1\) with observation shells at
\(kr_1=0.5\) and \(kr_2=5\), where \(k=\omega/c\). On \(S_{r_1}\), the reactive
integral \(Q(r_1)\) typically exceeds \(|P(r_1)|\), yielding
\(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_1)\gg 1\); phase winding and polarization ellipticity can be
large while exported power and axis torque remain small. On \(S_{r_2}\),
\(|P(r_2)|\gg |Q(r_2)|\) restores conservation-compatible transport
interpretation, and \(\mathcal{C}_\tau\gg 1\) signals that torque channels become
measurably active only after the reactive shell is crossed
\cite{stratton1941}. This two-surface protocol is the
measurement counterpart of the regime indices \(\chi\) and \(\chi_\Omega\) from
Section~\ref{sec:ch01.2.4}.

Define active-power and reactive-power surface functionals
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex64-power-functionals}
P(r)=\int_{S_r}\Re\!\left\{\mathbf{S}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\right\}dS,\qquad
Q(r)=\int_{S_r}\Im\!\left\{\mathbf{S}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\right\}dS,
\end{equation}
where \(\mathbf{S}=\tfrac{1}{2}\E\times\H^*\) is the complex Poynting vector
\cite{poynting1884} and \(\Im\{\cdot\}\) extracts imaginary part. The first integral
measures net exported power; the second measures reactive circulation associated
with local storage exchange.

To compare regimes on one normalized axis, define reactive ratio
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex64-reactive-ratio}
\mathcal{R}_Q(r)=\frac{|Q(r)|}{|P(r)|+\epsilon_P},
\qquad \epsilon_P>0.
\end{equation}
Reactive-dominant behavior corresponds to \(\mathcal{R}_Q\gg 1\), while
radiative-dominant behavior corresponds to \(\mathcal{R}_Q\ll 1\). This scalar
ratio makes regime classification operationally testable at each observation
surface.

For a torque channel about \(\hat{\mathbf{z}}\), define
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex64-torque-contrast}
\mathcal{C}_\tau
=
\frac{|\tau_z(r_2)|}{|\tau_z(r_1)|+\epsilon_\tau},
\qquad
\epsilon_\tau>0.
\end{equation}
The numerator and denominator are measured torque magnitudes on outer and inner
surfaces; \(\epsilon_\tau\) is a small regularization constant preventing division
singularity. When \(Q(r_1)\gg P(r_1)\) and \(P(r_2)\gg |Q(r_2)|\), one typically
obtains \(\mathcal{C}_\tau\gg 1\): near-zone angular structure is visually rich
yet weakly transport-capable, while far-zone structure carries measurable torque.

Measurement channels at the two surfaces are written
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex64-surface-channel-model}
y_{P,k}=K_{P,k}P(r_k)+n_{P,k},\qquad
y_{Q,k}=K_{Q,k}Q(r_k)+n_{Q,k},\qquad
y_{\tau,k}=K_{\tau,k}\tau_z(r_k)+n_{\tau,k},
\end{equation}
for \(k\in\{1,2\}\), where \(K_{\bullet,k}\) are calibration factors and
\(n_{\bullet,k}\) are channel disturbances. Equation
\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-surface-channel-model} ensures that regime claims are tied to
calibrated outputs rather than inferred from qualitative field appearance.

Define regime-gated transport efficiency
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex64-gated-efficiency}
\eta_{\tau}(r_k)
=
\frac{|\tau_z(r_k)|}{P(r_k)/\omega+\epsilon_\eta}
\cdot
\frac{1}{1+\mathcal{R}_Q(r_k)},
\qquad \epsilon_\eta>0.
\end{equation}
The factor \(1/(1+\mathcal{R}_Q)\) suppresses apparent efficiency in reactive
regimes where local circulation dominates exported transport.

Surface-to-surface trend consistency is captured by
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex64-trend-consistency}
\mathcal{T}_{12}
=
\frac{\left|\eta_{\tau}(r_2)-\eta_{\tau}(r_1)\right|}
     {\eta_{\tau}(r_2)+\epsilon_t},
\qquad \epsilon_t>0.
\end{equation}
Large \(\mathcal{T}_{12}\) indicates strong regime transition in transport
effectiveness, which is expected when \(r_1\) is reactive-dominant and \(r_2\) is
radiative-dominant.

\paragraph{Representative channel values.}
For a center-fed dipole at \(f=1\,\mathrm{GHz}\) (\(k=20.96\,\mathrm{rad/m}\)), take
calibrated reads \(y_{P,1}=0.05\,\mathrm{W}\), \(y_{Q,1}=0.40\,\mathrm{W}\) on
\(S_{r_1}\) with \(kr_1=0.5\), giving \(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_1)\approx 8\gg 1\) and
\(\eta_\tau(r_1)\approx 0\) from Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-gated-efficiency}. On
\(S_{r_2}\) with \(kr_2=5\), suppose \(y_{P,2}=0.85\,\mathrm{W}\),
\(y_{Q,2}=0.04\,\mathrm{W}\), so \(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_2)\approx 0.05\ll 1\). If
\(|\tau_z(r_1)|=0.2\,\mathrm{nN\,m}\) and \(|\tau_z(r_2)|=4.5\,\mathrm{nN\,m}\),
then \(\mathcal{C}_\tau\approx 22\) and \(\mathcal{T}_{12}\) is order unity, confirming
regime transition rather than measurement noise. Failing to report \(Q(r)\) alongside
\(P(r)\) would mislabel the inner surface as torque-capable based on phase texture alone
\cite{stratton1941,poynting1884}.

\paragraph{Chu quality factor and reactive shell diagnosis.}
Linking Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.2.4}, the Chu definition
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.chu-q-definition} compares stored energy to radiated power. On
\(S_{r_1}\) with \(kr_1=0.5\), illustrative dipole data give
\(|Q(r_1)|\gg P(r_1)\) and \(\chi(r_1)\gg 1\); the equivalent
\(Q_{\mathrm{Chu}}\) lower bound Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.chu-q-lower-bound} with
\(ka\approx 0.16\) yields \(Q_{\mathrm{LB}}\gtrsim 240\), signaling a
storage-dominated shell. On \(S_{r_2}\) with \(kr_2=5\),
\(\chi(r_2)\ll 1\) and \(Q_{\mathrm{Chu}}\) approaches its asymptotic minimum for
the dominant mode. The two-shell protocol therefore aligns three independent
diagnostics---\(\mathcal{R}_Q\), \(\chi(r)\), and \(Q_{\mathrm{Chu}}\)---on the same
classification: inner data are storage-diagnostic; outer data are export-diagnostic
\cite{chu1948}.

\paragraph{Step-by-step shell comparison with closure arithmetic.}
\emph{Step 6---Chu consistency.}
Verify \(2\omega\langle U\rangle_{\mathrm{st}}/P_{\mathrm{rad}}\ge Q_{\mathrm{LB}}\)
on each shell using Table~\ref{tab:ch1.regime-numeric-dipole} as order-of-magnitude
guide. On \(S_{r_1}\), violation of export interpretation is expected; on
\(S_{r_2}\), consistency confirms radiative placement.
\emph{Step 7---Joint criterion.}
With \(R_{Q,\min}=2\), \(R_{Q,\max}=0.2\), \(C_{\tau,\min}=5\), and measured
\(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_1)=8\), \(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_2)=0.05\), \(\mathcal{C}_\tau=22\),
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-regime-admissibility} yields \(\mathcal{D}_{64}=1\) when
\(\mathcal{D}_{63}=1\) and \(\mathcal{T}_{12}\le T_{12,\max}\). Failure of any
single inequality---for example \(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_2)\gg 1\) because the outer
shell was placed too close---forces reclassification without invalidating Maxwell
theory \cite{chu1948,stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Worked comparison: Allen-type beam on inner versus outer shell.}
A paraxial beam with \(\mathrm{LG}_{0}^{1}\) structure \cite{allen1992} illuminates
the same dipole source. On \(S_{r_1}\) with \(kr_1=0.5\), strong azimuthal phase
gradient yields large \(\mathcal{V}_\phi\) but \(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_1)\gg 1\) and
\(|\tau_z(r_1)|\ll|\tau_z(r_2)|\). On \(S_{r_2}\) with \(kr_2=5\),
\(\mathcal{R}_Q(r_2)\ll 1\) and \(\eta_\tau(r_2)\) exceeds \(\eta_\tau(r_1)\) by
more than an order of magnitude. Poynting diagnostics \cite{poynting1884} on the
outer shell confirm export-compatible power \(P(r_2)\); inner-shell reactive
circulation \(Q(r_1)\) must not be interpreted as orbital transport
\cite{allen1992}.

\begin{figure}[t]
\centering
\ChOneFigGeo{%
\begin{tikzpicture}[ch1geo, scale=0.90]
  \fill (0,0) circle (2pt);
  \draw[ch1shellO] (0,0) circle (1.15);
  \draw[ch1shellB] (0,0) circle (2.35);
  \draw[->, thick, orange!85!black] (0.8,0.18) arc (12:372:0.8);
  \draw[->, very thick, blue!70!black] (2.05,0) -- (2.55,0);
  \node[ch1box, fill=gray!10, align=center, minimum width=30mm] at (0,3.15)
    {Source block:\\centre-fed\\$\lambda/2$ dipole};
  \node[ch1box, fill=orange!12, orange!85!black, align=center, minimum width=38mm]
    at (-4.35,0.45) {Inner-shell block:\\reactive shell $S_{r_1}$,\\$kr_1=0.5$,\ $\mathcal{R}_Q(r_1)\gg 1$;\\storage circulation};
  \node[ch1box, fill=blue!12, blue!70!black, align=center, minimum width=38mm]
    at (4.35,0.45) {Outer-shell block:\\radiative shell $S_{r_2}$,\\$kr_2=5$,\ $\mathcal{R}_Q(r_2)\ll 1$;\\outward power export};
  \node[ch1box, fill=gray!10, align=center, minimum width=52mm] at (0,-3.15)
    {Readout block:\\shell channels $(y_P,y_Q,y_\tau)$;\\contrast $\mathcal{C}_\tau$,\ efficiency $\eta_\tau$;\\closure $\mathcal{D}_{64}=1$};
\end{tikzpicture}%
}
\caption{Worked-problem geometry for Subsection~\ref{sec:ch01.6.4}: four labelled blocks identify the dipole source, reactive inner shell $S_{r_1}$, radiative outer shell $S_{r_2}$, and shell readout/closure protocol.}
\label{fig:ch1.ex64-regime-comparison}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.ex64-regime-comparison} encodes the experimental moral of
Table~\ref{tab:ch1.regime-numeric-dipole}: stand-off is a physical parameter, not a
display choice. Angular-structure claims must name the shell at which channels were
read and report \(\mathcal{R}_Q\) alongside torque.

The worked-case admissibility criterion is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.ex64-regime-admissibility}
\mathcal{D}_{64}=1
\iff
\Big(
\mathcal{D}_{63}=1,\
\mathcal{R}_Q(r_1)\ge R_{Q,\min},\
\mathcal{R}_Q(r_2)\le R_{Q,\max},\
\mathcal{C}_\tau\ge C_{\tau,\min},\
\mathcal{T}_{12}\le T_{12,\max}
\Big),
\end{equation}
where \(R_{Q,\min}\), \(R_{Q,\max}\), \(C_{\tau,\min}\), and \(T_{12,\max}\) are
declared thresholds. Equation~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-regime-admissibility} ensures that
reactive/radiative labeling and torque-contrast interpretation are jointly
consistent.

\begin{proposition}[Reactive-radiative discrimination criterion]
\label{prop:ch1.ex64-regime-discrimination}
The surface-comparison conclusion of this subsection is physically admissible only
if \(\mathcal{D}_{64}=1\).
\end{proposition}
\noindent\textit{Proof sketch.}
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-power-functionals} defines active/reactive channels,
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-reactive-ratio} defines regime class,
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-torque-contrast} and
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-gated-efficiency} define transport comparison, and
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.ex64-regime-admissibility} imposes thresholded closure. Their
conjunction establishes the criterion.

This comparison assumes identical origin/axis declarations, stationary harmonic
operation, and negligible environmental scattering between \(S_{r_1}\) and
\(S_{r_2}\). Strong inhomogeneous media or multipath contamination can distort
\(P,Q,\tau_z\) trend comparison and require full propagation compensation
\cite{stratton1941}.

The worked sequence of Section~\ref{sec:ch01.6} is therefore complete: radiation
torque conservation, phase-only counterexample, gauge-sensitivity check, and
reactive/radiative discrimination are all established in operational form.
\paragraph{Section 1.6 outcome and bridge.}
Section~\ref{sec:ch01.6} verifies conservation torque prediction, phase-only
counterexamples, gauge-sensitive local maps, and reactive-radiative surface
comparison under the full reporting protocol. Section~\ref{sec:ch01.7} consolidates
established results and states the forward inheritance map into Chapter~2.


\section{Chapter Summary and Forward Map}
\label{sec:ch01.7}

\emph{Chapter summary} records verified Level~I outcomes---Maxwell law, conservation,
transport screens, gauge discipline, and measurement limits---without re-displaying their
proofs. \emph{Forward map} states what Chapter~2 may import by reference and what remains
deferred to Chapters~3--4 realizability theory \cite{stratton1941,harrington2001}.
Section~\ref{sec:ch01.7} is the governed transition layer: it closes Level~I of
Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.three-level-hierarchy} and points to radiation operators
(Chapter~2), eigenfield representations (Chapter~3), and finite-source realizability
(Chapter~4).

Section~\ref{sec:ch01.7} closes Chapter~\ref{ch:01} by listing verified outcomes,
declaring deferred topic boundaries, and stating the inheritance map for
Chapter~2. No new theorem content is introduced; the section is a governed transition
layer only.


\subsection{Results established in Chapter 1}
\label{sec:ch01.7.1}
% TOC tag: [DEFER]

\emph{Results established} collects theorem-level outcomes that survived Maxwell law,
transport screening, covariance discipline, gauge bounds, and measurement limits.
The ledger is compact by design: proofs remain in their home subsections, and
Chapter~2 imports by reference only \cite{stratton1941}.

Chapter~\ref{ch:01} closes the Maxwell-to-measurement chain required before
Chapter~\ref{ch:02}. Downstream material inherits by reference only through
Eq.~\eqref{eq:ch1.master-admissibility-chain} and
Table~\ref{tab:ch1.admissibility-corollaries}. The chapter-level criterion
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.inheritance-admissibility}
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ch1}}=1
\iff
\left(
\mathcal{D}_{J}=1,\
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{org}}=1,\
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{g}}=1,\
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{op}}=1
\right),
\end{equation}
packages transport, covariance, gauge, and operational admissibility. Let
\(\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{ch1}}\) denote the set of results established in
Sections~\ref{sec:ch01.1}--\ref{sec:ch01.6} under
\(\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ch1}}=1\). Every reported quantity must carry a report class from
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.report-class-lock}
\mathcal{Q}\in
\{\text{direct observable},\ \text{constrained surrogate},\ \text{inference-only}\},
\end{equation}
as fixed in Sections~\ref{sec:ch01.5}--\ref{sec:ch01.6}
\cite{stratton1941}.


\subsection{Concepts deferred to Chapters 2-4 and Volume II}
\label{sec:ch01.7.2}
% TOC tag: [DEFER]

\emph{Concepts deferred} are topics whose proofs require operator domains
(Chapter~2), representation closure (Chapter~3), or finite-source realizability and
truncation (Chapter~4). Listing them here prevents premature re-derivation in
Level~I prose and keeps the three-level hierarchy of
Figure~\ref{fig:ch1.three-level-hierarchy} intellectually honest
\cite{stratton1941,harrington2001}.

No theorem is introduced here. Chapter~2 owns operator-domain and radiation-mapping
formalism; Chapter~3 owns representation-theoretic closure for angular operators;
Chapter~4 owns source realizability and truncation limits. Forward chapters must
satisfy
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.defer-topic-rule}
\begin{aligned}
\mathcal{X}\in\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{defer}}
&\iff
\mathcal{X}\ \text{requires operator-domain proof from Ch.2} \\
&\ \vee\ \mathcal{X}\ \text{requires representation closure from Ch.3} \\
&\ \vee\ \mathcal{X}\ \text{requires realizability/truncation proof from Ch.4},
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.defer-reporting-lock}
\mathcal{X}\in\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{defer}}
\Longrightarrow
\text{use by forward reference only; no local re-derivation in Ch.1}.
\end{equation}
\cite{stratton1941}.


\subsection{Bridge to Chapter 2}
\label{sec:ch01.7.3}
% TOC tag: [DEFER]

\emph{Bridge to Chapter 2} names the inheritance map: which Level~I certificates
\(\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ch1}}=1\) must hold before radiation operators, Green
mappings, and source-to-field actions are developed without reopening Maxwell proofs
\cite{stratton1941}.

Chapter~2 begins from the closed inheritance base assembled in
Sections~\ref{sec:ch01.1}--\ref{sec:ch01.6}: Maxwell conservation, transport
admissibility, covariance discipline, gauge-observability screening, and
channel-level measurement interpretation. These results are imported by reference;
Chapter~2 may develop operator domains, source-to-field maps, and Green-function
actions without reopening Chapter~1 proofs. Compatibility is encoded by
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.bridge-inheritance-map}
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{bridge}}(\mathcal{Y})=1
\iff
\left(
\mathcal{Y}\ \text{is compatible with}\ \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{ch1}}
\ \wedge\
\mathcal{Y}\ \text{adds no recursive proof of}\ \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{ch1}}
\right),
\end{equation}
screened by
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ch1.bridge-compatibility-criteria}
\mathcal{Y}\prec\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{ch1}}
\iff
\left(
\mathcal{D}_{J}=1,\
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{org}}=1,\
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{g}}=1,\
\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{op}}=1
\right)\ \text{remain unviolated by }\mathcal{Y},
\end{equation}
with inherited \(\mathcal{D}_{J}\), \(\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{org}}\),
\(\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{g}}\), and \(\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{op}}\) criteria
\cite{stratton1941}.

\paragraph{Section 1.7 terminal summary.}
Chapter~\ref{ch:01} now stands as the sole foundational basis for the
Maxwell-conservation-gauge-observability structure used by subsequent chapters.
Chapter~2 inherits this base by reference and develops operator-domain machinery
without recursive re-derivation.
